# CHANGELOG

Machine-friendly drop ledger for SW_MUSH. One entry per delivered
drop. Companion to `TODO.json` (forward-looking) and
`sw_d6_mush_architecture_v51.md` (narrative ground truth).

---

> **Older entries archived.** The 2026-05-24 seed drop through 2026-06-18 live in
> [`CHANGELOG_ARCHIVE.md`](CHANGELOG_ARCHIVE.md) to keep this file small. Recent
> drops (2026-06-19 onward) are below.

### 2026-06-24 — World content: Kuat industrial & civic ambient population — *drop ambient-kuat-industrial-civic* (Sonnet loop)
Six non-hostile ambient/flavor NPCs filling four KDY orbital-ring and Kuat City rooms with no prior ambient coverage. The Pressure Drop Cantina x2: Veela Torsk (Human, 31yr Grade-7 hull plating specialist occupying the end stool at KDY's forty-year-old worker cantina; has opinions about Republic contractors cutting stress-tolerance corners; starship_repair 5D+1, capital_ship_repair 4D+2) and Jarec Mave (Human, Bay Seven welding crew supervisor running a three-way shift handoff between ales; command 3D+1, capital_ship_repair 3D+2). Ring Residential Block x2: Narra Kessel (Human, 72yr three-generation ring resident tending the negotiated community garden bays; her grandfather helped install the original environmental seals; willpower 4D) and Tov Saren (Sullustan, 8yr overnight calibration tech coming off a twelve-hour Venator turbolaser-emplacement tolerance run; sensors 4D+1, navigation 3D). Machine Shops x1: Pressa Velk (Human, one of 42 KDY-certified master fabricators working precision guidance housings for Venator turbolaser batteries; the certification board has not been expedited despite war demands; capital_ship_repair 5D, TEC 4D). Kuat City - Mercantile Forum x1: Heset Andrim (Human, House Andrim junior observer in the public gallery watching the House Andrim / House Purkis subcontracting session through gallery glass; bureaucracy 4D, persuasion 3D+1). All six hostile: false, no special-reward markers, no era violations, original characters, Q1-compliant (House Andrim named in room desc; Heset Andrim is original, non-canonical). Wired into era.yaml content_refs.npcs. New test file `tests/test_drop_ambient_kuat_industrial_civic.py` (34 passed including hygiene + era_guard). Data + test only; no engine/schema change; no faucet/sink.

### 2026-06-24 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: spacer-quest onboarding funnel — *drop t319-spacer-quest-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The 30-step "From Dust to Stars" new-player chain (`engine/spacer_quest.py`) had ZERO telemetry. Its per-step credit faucet already rides `credit_flow` under the `spacer_quest` tag, but those isolated ledger rows can't be rejoined offline into the **onboarding funnel** — how many players START the chain vs the last step they reach (the drop-off curve), how many reach grand COMPLETE, and the per-step pay. This is exactly the new-player retention + onboarding-economy signal the T3.19 sink exists to capture (is a phase a wall? is a step's pay too low to bother finishing?). New `_emit_spacer_telemetry(phase, char, qs, *, step_id, credits, title, phase_gate)` helper (mirrors the engine chains' `chain_reward` step/graduation events; the spacer quest lives in the char attr blob, not the chain engine, so it needs its own emitter): ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `spacer_quest` event per transition, tagged by `phase` — **`start`** (chain auto-started, at the `_maybe_start_chain` seam, after the prereq+idempotence gates and the state persist), **`step`** (a step 1-29 completed, at the end of `_complete_step`, tagging the macro `quest_phase` 1-5, the `credits` faucet, and the `phase_gate` transitions), and **`complete`** (step 30 grand completion). The step emit sits at the function tail AFTER the advance, so step 27's affordability gate (which `return`s early when the player can't afford the 8000cr ship) correctly does NOT count a can't-afford attempt. Sampling honours the new `telemetry.spacer_quest_sample` tunable (default 1.0 — a once-per-player low-frequency lifecycle; sampling it down would blur the very drop-off curve it exists to show; documented in `data/tunables.yaml`). Buffer-only + offline-flushed → can never disturb the quest step it observes. Observe-only: no engine logic change, no schema, no new faucet/sink (`adjust_credits` call sites untouched), era-clean, funnel-respecting. New `tests/test_t319_spacer_quest_telemetry.py` (17 tests: per-phase field schema + dropped zero/false fields + None-id coercion; `start` fires only with prereq met, not already-running, not on a wrong trigger; `step` emits one event with the faucet matching the ledger leg; the phase-gate step tags the post-advance transition; step 30 emits `complete` + the +1 CP grand-completion lands; `telemetry.spacer_quest_sample=0` suppresses the event but not the reward; a raising sink never disturbs the step; source-wiring + tunable-doc drift pins). Gate green (spacer-quest + tunables-foundation + hygiene + smoke foundation, 81 passed).

### 2026-06-24 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: vanity-title prestige lifecycle — *drop t319-title-lifecycle-telemetry* (Opus loop)
**Authoritative T3.19 telemetry breadth** on the vanity-title prestige sink (`engine/titles.py`). The purchase debit already rides `credit_flow` under the `vanity_title` tag (plus `vanity_title_refund` on a failed-and-refunded buy), but those isolated rows can't be rejoined offline into the **prestige lifecycle** — which of the 8 price tiers actually sell (2k Wayfarer → 400k Luminary of the Core), how purchased prestige compares to *earned* prestige, or how much veteran credit the sink soaks up against take-up. New `_emit_title_telemetry(action, char_id, amount, **extra)` helper (mirrors the `gear_insurance` / `debt` lifecycle emitters): ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `vanity_title` event per transition tagged by `action` — **`purchase`** (the sink — `amount = -cost`, plus the price-tier index `tier` 0–7 and the `owned` count after the buy) and **`grant`** (an EARNED deed-reward title, `amount = 0`, no credits move; no `tier`). Both seams sit AFTER the credit move + the owned-set persist both succeed, so a failed-and-refunded buy (or any refusal — unknown / already-owned / insufficient / concurrent-overdraw) emits **nothing** — never a phantom prestige signal. Sampling honours the new `telemetry.title_sample` tunable (default 1.0 — a deliberate, low-frequency buy/earn). The signal for tuning the `VANITY_TITLES` cost curve: a dead top tier is priced past reach; everyone parked on the cheap tiers means the sink is too shallow. New `tests/test_t319_title_telemetry.py` (28: one event per successful purchase/grant with the right action + signed amount + tier + owned count; every refusal + the persist-fail-refund emit nothing; the str→int id coercion + None-field drop; sample=0 suppresses the event but not the buy; a raising sink never disturbs the purchase/grant; the seam wiring + event-type + tunable-doc pins). 42 title + telemetry tests green. Engine + data + test only; no schema; no new faucet/sink (pure additive observation on an existing sink); era-clean; funnel-respecting.

### 2026-06-24 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: Hutt-debt payment lifecycle — *drop t319-debt-lifecycle-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The weekly Hutt-debt auto-debit (`engine/debt.process_all_debts`) already logs its credit sink under the `debt_payment` ledger tag, but those isolated `credit_flow` rows can't be rejoined offline into the debt *lifecycle* — the on-schedule-payment vs missed rate, the miss→enforcer-escalation rate, and the time-to-payoff distribution. Added ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `debt` telemetry event per weekly transition, tagged by `action`: `payment` (a partial weekly payment, with `principal_remaining` + `total_paid`), `payoff` (the final payment that cleared the principal), and `missed` (insufficient credits — `amount` 0, `payments_missed` count, plus an `escalation` tag of `warning`/`enforcer` derived from the count). New `_emit_debt()` helper mirrors the established gear-insurance/commissary emitter shape (int-coerce char_id, drop None fields, `telemetry.debt_sample` keep-rate default 1.0, swallow-everything fail-open). The two emit seams sit AFTER the `adjust_credits` sink + attr-persist on the payment path and OUTSIDE the `if sess:` session gate on the miss path, so the lifecycle is recorded even for an offline debtor (the comlink/title side-effects stay session-gated, unchanged). No behavior change, no schema change, no new faucet/sink, era-clean; the signal directly tunes `DEBT_WEEKLY_PAYMENT` (500cr) + the warning/enforcer miss thresholds. Documented `telemetry.debt_sample` in `data/tunables.yaml` (purely additive). New `tests/test_t319_debt_telemetry.py` (19 tests: per-action schema + envelope, ledger-leg match, escalation tracks the missed count, no-debt/zero-principal/not-due/empty-attrs emit nothing, offline-debtor still recorded, sample-tunable honoured, broken-sink-never-disturbs-the-payment fail-open, helper unit + source-pin seams). Gate green (61 incl. hygiene + smoke foundation).

### 2026-06-24 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: gear-insurance policy lifecycle — *drop t319-gear-insurance-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Closes the gear-insurance economy seam (`engine/gear_insurance.py`, the `+insure` loadout-protection sink). The premium debit already rides `credit_flow` per-tag (`gear_insurance_premium` / `gear_insurance_premium_refund`), but those isolated rows can't be rejoined offline into the policy *lifecycle* — the buy→cancel voluntary-churn rate or the premium-sink volume against take-up. By design this module has NO payout (a payout would be a suicide-faucet, see the module docstring), so the lone tuning lever is `GEAR_INSURANCE_PREMIUM`: too cheap → everyone insures and the consensual gear-loss sink the lawless/contested zones rest on erodes; too dear → dead weight. New `_emit_gear_insurance(action, char_id, amount, **extra)` helper (mirrors `housing._emit_housing` / `dens._emit_den`): one fail-open, sample-tunable `gear_insurance` event at each lifecycle transition — **purchase** (`amount=-GEAR_INSURANCE_PREMIUM`, the premium sink, tagged `premium`) and **cancel** (`amount=0`, no credits move — the premium is a pure sink). Wired at the two success seams in `purchase_gear_insurance` / `cancel_gear_insurance` AFTER the credit leg + flag persist both land, so every refusal (already insured / insufficient funds / charge-fail / persist-fail-and-refund / not-insured / stale-cache / cancel-persist-fail) emits nothing — never a phantom policy signal. The death-consume leg moves no credits and lives in `engine/death.py` (avoid-lane), so it is intentionally NOT emitted; this emitter covers the buy/cancel side. Sampling honours new tunable `telemetry.gear_insurance_sample` (default 1.0; documented in `data/tunables.yaml`). Buffer-only + offline-flushed → can never disturb the buy/cancel it observes. Observe-only: no engine logic change, no schema, no faucet/sink, `adjust_credits` call sites untouched, era-clean. 22 tests (`tests/test_t319_gear_insurance_telemetry.py`): the two transitions driven through the REAL `purchase_gear_insurance`/`cancel_gear_insurance` against a recording stub (one event each, right action + signed amount); the six refusal/failure branches each emit nothing; `telemetry.gear_insurance_sample=0.0` suppresses the event but not the buy/flag; fail-open under a raising sink (both buy + cancel still land); the helper schema + None-id coercion + None-extra-drop; source-wiring + tunable-registration drift pins. Existing `test_gear_insurance.py` / `test_insurance_debt_gate.py` / `test_t319_den_telemetry.py` all still green (97 in the gate).

### 2026-06-24 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: PvP player-bounty economy lifecycle — *drop t319-pc-bounty-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The PvP player-bounty system (PG.2, `parser/pc_bounty_commands.py`) is a closed credit loop **distinct from the NPC `bounty_board` faucet** (already telemetered): a poster STAKES escrow + burns a 10% posting fee (sink); a BH Guild hunter is PAID 80% on fulfilment with 20% sunk to the Guild treasury (faucet); cancel/void/expire leak escrow back to contributors minus the already-sunk fee. Every credit leg already lands in `credit_log` per-tag (`bounty_post` / `bh_bounty_payout` / `bounty_*_refund` / `bounty_expire_refund` …), but **nothing rejoins offline into the contract lifecycle** — the post→fulfil vs post→cancel/expire funnel, the escrow-amount distribution against `MAX_BOUNTY`, and the posting/cancel fee-burn volume. New `_emit_pc_bounty(action, char_id, amount, **extra)` helper (mirrors `dens._emit_den` / `housing._emit_housing`): one fail-open, sample-tunable `pc_bounty` event at each of the **six** lifecycle transitions — `post` (`_do_new_post`, amount=−total_debit, escrow/fee), `stack` (`_do_stack`, +total_escrow), `cancel` (`_handle_cancel`, amount=refund_pool, fee=cancel_fee), `fulfill` (`_handle_fulfill`, amount=payout, sunk=20% Guild treasury), `void` (`_handle_void`, full refund, char_id 0), `expire` (`run_pc_bounty_expiry_tick`, per-bounty stake refund, char_id 0). Each emit is wired **after the DB write / refund leg before return**, so every refusal (insufficient credits, self-target, < `MIN_BOUNTY`, unknown BH, nothing-to-cancel, no-expiry) emits nothing — never a phantom contract signal. New knob `telemetry.pc_bounty_sample` (default 1.0 — a deliberate PvP act is low-frequency + high-value). Observe-only: no credit movement, schema, or faucet/sink change; `adjust_credits` call sites untouched; era-clean. New `tests/test_t319_pc_bounty_telemetry.py` (27: helper schema + None-drop + sign convention + sampling + fail-open; the six transitions driven against a real in-memory `Database` via the live `BountyCommand`/`AdminBountyCommand`/tick; refusal-emits-nothing for each; the load-bearing "broken sink never disturbs the post/fulfil it observes" contract; source-wiring + tunable-registration drift pins). `test_pg2_pc_bounty_session{1,2}` + `test_qa_bounty_2026_06_23` + `test_t319_den_telemetry` all still green (144 in the gate).

### 2026-06-24 — World content: Coruscant civic core and government hall mob grind expansion — *drop mob-grind-coruscant-civic-government* (Sonnet loop)
Six roaming hostile NPCs seeded across six previously uncovered Coruscant rooms — completing coverage of the Senate District civic core and the Mosaic Hotel. Rooms covered: Galactic Senate Building Exterior Plaza x1 (Zabrak CIS spotter, concealed_blaster), Galactic Senate Building Public Lobby x1 (Duros data broker, hold_out_blaster), Chancellor's Avenue x1 (Aqualish extortionist, blaster_pistol), Grand Reception Hall x1 (Twi'lek document thief, concealed_blaster), Legislative Borough x1 (Human CIS asset, blaster_pistol), The Mosaic Hotel x1 (Nikto fugitive, blaster_pistol). Thematic premise: The Senate District's clone trooper presence concentrates on government entry-points and dignitary routes, not the surrounding civic fabric; the Senate Building's plaza and lobby draw thousands of political observers daily — ideal cover for intelligence operatives marking senators; the Legislative Borough's GAR logistics center is a high-value Separatist intelligence target; Chancellor's Avenue's patrols leave a 12-minute rotation gap that an Aqualish protection ring has exploited for 16 months; the Grand Reception Hall's state receptions give a Twi'lek document thief credentials to work the crowd; the Mosaic Hotel's discretion harbors a Nikto bounty hunter with one bad contract and three days until his transport. All satisfy `is_huntable_mob()` (hostile=true, none of the special-reward markers). Original characters, era-clean (~20 BBY), WEG D6 stats grounded in sibling CW senate-district baselines (unverified vs WEG40120 PDF absent in tree). Wired into era.yaml content_refs.npcs. New test file `tests/test_mob_grind_coruscant_civic_government.py` (13 test functions, 28 assertions pass). Data + test only; no engine/schema change; no faucet/sink.

### 2026-06-24 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: Hutt-cartel sabacc-den lifecycle — *drop t319-den-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Closes the last uninstrumented criminal-economy seam: the cartel sabacc-den lifecycle. The setup-cost credit leg already rides `credit_flow` (`adjust_credits` tags `sabacc_den_setup`) and the den *rake* faucet is captured by the sabacc `gamble` emitter, but neither rejoins offline into the den **lifecycle** — the per-org establish→abandon churn or the setup-sink volume. New `engine/dens._emit_den(action, char_id, amount, **extra)` helper (mirrors `engine/housing._emit_housing`): one fail-open, sample-tunable `den` event at each lifecycle transition — **establish** (`amount=-DEN_SETUP_COST`, the 10k sink) and **abandon** (`amount=0`, no credits move), each tagged with `org_id`/`org_code`/`room_id`. Wired at the two success seams in `establish_den` / `abandon_den` (after the DB write, before the return) so a refusal or write-failure refund emits nothing — never a phantom signal. Sampling honours new tunable `telemetry.den_sample` (default 1.0; den acts are very low-frequency). Buffer-only + offline-flushed → can never disturb the establish/abandon it observes. The rake-faucet/setup-sink pair is now fully observable on `@economy` for tuning `DEN_SETUP_COST` / `DEN_ESTABLISH_MIN_RANK` post-launch. No schema change, no faucet/sink change, era-clean. 24 tests (`tests/test_t319_den_telemetry.py`); existing `test_a5_dens.py` still green.

### 2026-06-24 — Fix L2: Force-sensitive 0D lockout — key-presence rule + actionable +teach message — *drop l2-force-0d-lockout-fix* (Sonnet loop)
A Force-sensitive character whose `control`/`sense`/`alter` attributes are all `"0D"` (new player who hasn't trained yet) was silently locked out of ALL Force commands with the confusing message "You lack the Force skill(s) needed: Control. You must develop Control to use control_pain." — even though they correctly self-identify as Force-sensitive. Root cause: two-part. (1) `engine/character.py` `load_from_db` used `if not pool.is_zero(): char.force_sensitive = True` for force-attr key presence, but the CLAUDE.md architecture invariant says key presence → force-sensitive regardless of value. Fixed: the `is_zero()` guard removed — any key in the attrs blob sets `force_sensitive = True`. (2) `parser/force_commands.py` `ForceCommand.execute` printed the confusing "lack the skill" message. Fixed: message now reads "You are Force-sensitive but Control is untrained (0D). Force skills are raised through a master/apprentice bond — ask a Jedi Master to use +teach." — this is correct guidance (the `train` command explicitly rejects control/sense/alter and redirects to `+teach`). No schema change, no faucet/sink, era-clean. 10 tests (`tests/test_l2_force_0d_lockout_fix.py`): key-presence with all-0D → force_sensitive=True; no keys → False; partial key → True; 0D roundtrip preserved; ForceCommand gives +teach message not "lack" message; non-FS still gets right message; unknown power still gets right message; single-skill 0D pinned; no-args → Usage. All 89 existing Force+character+hygiene+smoke pass.

### 2026-06-23 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: player-healer medical-services economy — *drop t319-medical-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The player-to-player heal-for-hire loop (`parser/medical_commands.py`) is both a credit **sink** (the patient pays) and **faucet** (the healer earns): a successful `healaccept` moves credits through `adjust_credits(..., "medical")` twice (patient debit + healer credit). But those two `credit_flow` rows can't be rejoined offline into a single healer→patient service transaction, and — the load-bearing gap — the **partial** (`margin >= -4`, "bleeding stabilised", no charge) and **failed/fumbled** treatments move NO credits at all, so `credit_flow` never sees them. So the medical-services market is mostly dark: the healer success rate (skill roll vs the wound-scaled `_HEAL_DIFFICULTY`), the rate-vs-wound-severity distribution, and the paid-for-nothing partial/fail share are all unreconstructable from the ledger — the direct signal for tuning `_HEAL_DIFFICULTY` and whether heal-for-hire is worth a player's credits vs a bacta tank. This drop adds ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `medical_treatment` event at the resolution seam of `HealAcceptCommand.execute` (after the success/partial/fail branches resolve), carrying coerced `healer_char`/`patient_char` ids, `room_id`, the `skill` used (first aid vs medicine), `difficulty`, the `roll`, the `outcome` (critical/success/partial/fail/fumble), `wound_before`→`wound_after`, the offered `rate`, and the credits actually `paid` (the `rate` on success, 0 otherwise). Three branch accumulators (`tele_outcome`/`tele_wound_after`/`tele_paid`, defaulting to the fail outcome) feed a single emit via a new module helper `_emit_medical_telemetry`, mirroring the entertainer/p2p-trade pattern. The insufficient-credits abort (the atomic `allow_negative=False` patient-debit guard returns None) returns early and is intentionally NOT recorded — no treatment completed there. Buffer-only + offline-flushed → zero gameplay behaviour; the emit is wrapped fail-open so a broken sink can never disturb the treatment it observes. Sampling honours new `telemetry.medical_sample` (default 1.0; documented in `data/tunables.yaml`). Observe-only: no engine logic change, no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean. 15 tests (`tests/test_t319_medical_telemetry.py`): the five outcomes driven end-to-end through the REAL `HealAcceptCommand.execute` against a recording stub DB + a controlled skill result (success one-step + payment, critical two-step heal, partial/fail are dark to `credit_flow`, fumble tagged), the debit-abort emits nothing, no-pending-offer / healer-left-room emit nothing, `telemetry.medical_sample=0.0` suppresses the event but not the heal-or-payment, fail-open under a raising sink, the helper schema + None-id coercion, and the seam/tunable source pins.

### 2026-06-23 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: entertainer (cantina) credit faucet — *drop t319-entertainer-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The entertainer perform loop (`parser/entertainer_commands.py`) is a cantina credit **faucet** — `perform` pays the social character via `adjust_credits(..., "entertainer")` — but that lone `credit_flow` row can't be rejoined offline into the depth that tunes the faucet: the **outcome split** (critical / success / partial / fail), the **fatigue-bumped difficulty** + `fatigue_count` (the diminishing-returns curve, design SRB.2), the **live-audience hub bonus** (A8 audience-weighting), or the **cantina-brawl 2x** flag. A partial-pay perform (25cr) and a flat-pay perform can log the same `entertainer` delta, so the outcome split is invisible without a dedicated emit — the direct signal for tuning the pay bounds (`_BASE_PAY`/`_CRIT_PAY`/`_PARTIAL_PAY`), the audience cap, the fatigue penalty, and the perform cooldowns. This drop adds ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `entertainer_perform` event at the post-dispatch seam (after the success/partial/fail branches resolve), carrying a coerced `char_id`, the `outcome`, the `payout` (matches the ledger leg exactly; 0 on fail), the `skill` used (persuasion vs musical instrument), `margin`, the fatigue-effective `difficulty`, `fatigue_count`, `audience` heads, and the `brawl`/`fumble` flags. Three branch accumulators (`perform_outcome`/`perform_payout`/`perform_audience`, defaulting to the fail outcome) feed a single emit, mirroring the sabacc `gamble` pattern. Buffer-only + offline-flushed → zero gameplay behaviour; the emit is wrapped fail-open so a broken sink can never disturb the performance it observes. Sampling honours new `telemetry.entertainer_sample` (default 1.0; documented in `data/tunables.yaml`). Observe-only: no engine logic change, no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean. 15 tests (`tests/test_t319_entertainer_telemetry.py`): the four outcome branches driven end-to-end against a recording stub DB, payout-matches-ledger cross-check, audience lift recorded, brawl 2x recorded, fatigue→difficulty recorded, musical-instrument skill recorded, `telemetry.entertainer_sample` honoured (0.0 suppresses the event but not the payout), fail-open under a raising sink, and the early-return zone-gate / cooldown paths emit nothing.

### 2026-06-23 -- UX-engagement design roadmap: 8 web-client depth-surfacing features planned + queued -- *drop ux-engagement-roadmap*
Design + roadmap drop (no engine code). Answers Brian's "other UI adds like the dice animation that make the game more engaging" with full, implementable design plans for EIGHT web-client features, all on one thesis: most of SW_MUSH's depth (Director faction turns, territory influence, the D6 combat wound/cover/initiative model, the questline engine, scenes/plots, the sheet) is real but **invisible in scrollback**, so the cheapest large engagement win is UI that *surfaces systems the engine already runs* -- "extend, don't add" at the client layer. New design-of-record `docs/design/ux_engagement_roadmap_2026-06-23.md` (preamble + per-feature sections: what/why + engagement lever, the shared add-vs-detract discipline [never gate pace/information; optional/toggleable; no phantom producers/verbs; lean payload on the existing HUD cadence; web-only/telnet-degrades], verified existing producers, honest gaps/new-work, an implementation sketch [engine extension + wire payload + client renderer + jsdom/engine tests], and phasing). Docs + TODO only; no engine/schema/faucet/sink change; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- REVIEW-FIX: post-gate adjudication of the fork+multihome batch -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Four fixes from the parallel invariant-auditor + code-reviewer pass and the threaded full-suite gate (13344 passed / 7 failed; the 7 triaged to pre-existing baseline-reds + these mine):
- **SPACE anomaly engage fail-OPEN -> fail-CLOSED (BLOCKER-class, both reviewers + `test_session38`):** `_engage_anomaly` had `success = (result is None) or ...`, so a skill-check EXCEPTION (`result=None`) granted a free credit award -- wrong direction for a faucet. Now `success = (result is not None) and result.success and not result.fumble` (an engine error blocks the payout + logs). The two `except Exception: pass` swallows in the same method are now `log.warning`/`log.debug` (clears the silent-except invariant).
- **HOUSING checkout_room recall-pointer corruption (MAJOR, code-reviewer):** the trailing unconditional `UPDATE characters SET home_room_id = NULL WHERE id = ?` ran after every checkout -- harmless single-home, but with multi-home now live, selling home #2 wiped a recall pointer aimed at home #1. Removed; the CONDITIONAL clear earlier in the function (`... WHERE home_room_id IN (deleted rooms)`) already covers the FK case correctly.
- **HOUSING get_homes phantom producer (MEDIUM, invariant-auditor):** `get_homes()` had only a test consumer. Wired the real consumer -- a new `housing list` subcommand (`_cmd_list`) that lists every home you own (up to 4), marking the recall home + the one you're standing in, so a multi-home owner can see what the location-aware management commands will act on.
- **ENV drink/hydrate command-gap (gate, `test_help_misc_command_gaps`):** the new `drink`/`hydrate` command had no help entry. Added `data/help/commands/drink.md` (`key: drink`, `aliases: [hydrate]`).
Gate triage (no regression introduced this session): the 3 chain-walkthrough fails are pre-existing flaky baseline-reds (my combat-exit `_combat_finished` + MoveCommand gate are byte-equivalent to `is_over` for solo 1v1, so cannot be the cause -- proven by analysis); cities cargo-tax is the pre-existing "watch item #7" (session never touched cargo/city-revenue); the mapgen `term_boundaries` seed is the parallel Nano loop's dirty working-tree write (committed HEAD is empty `{}`); `_verify_bacta.py` is an untracked throwaway probe (won't merge). New structural test pins the get_homes consumer. Parser + engine + help + test only; no schema.

### 2026-06-23 -- FIX: SPACE skill checks were never running (load_default doesn't exist) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
`parser/space_commands.py` called `sr.load_default()` at 8 sites, but `SkillRegistry` has no such method -> every call raised AttributeError. **Effect:** 3 commands (`+ship/install`, `order`, `transponder false`) silently NO-OP'd (generic error, nothing happened); 5 (scan / deepscan / hyperspace / salvage / customs) fell to a `result is None` fallback and **bypassed their skill gate entirely** -- free scans, guaranteed hyperspace jumps, free salvage loot, smugglers never caught at customs. Routed all 8 to the process-cached `get_cached_skill_registry()` (loaded once, off the event loop; difficulties unchanged -- the fix only makes the player's SKILL actually load). Swapping in a real result UNMASKED a second latent bug at deepscan + salvage: they read `result.critical` / `result.total`, attributes `SkillCheckResult` does NOT have (it has `.critical_success` / `.roll`) -- corrected, and made fail-CLOSED (an engine error no longer auto-succeeds the check). The valid `roll_result.total` (a roll_d6_pool result) and the MINE `result.critical` (a mining result) were correctly left alone. New `tests/test_fork_space_skill_registry_2026_06_23.py` (5: load_default gone, cached registry used, deepscan/salvage attrs correct + fail-closed, SkillCheckResult contract). 660 space-matching tests green (incl. smoke). Parser + test only; no schema; no difficulty/number changes.

Self-test green on the merged tree (also confirms the merge boots + serves the full new-player flow in a real browser). ### 2026-06-23 -- FORK: HOUSING.single_home_only -> multi-home (own up to 4, location-aware ops) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Resolves the single-home cap (Brian: "4 homes is good"). `purchase_home` BLOCKED any 2nd Tier-3 home ("You already own a home") and the `MAX_TIER3_TOTAL` / `MAX_TIER3_PER_PLANET` constants were dead. **Now:** own up to `MAX_TIER3_TOTAL` (4) Tier-3 homes -- the global block is replaced by a total-cap count checked AFTER lot validation (so an invalid lot still returns "Invalid lot." first), and the eviction step is guarded to `existing["tier"] < 3` so buying another home rolls up only a Tier 1/2 RENTAL, never an existing Tier-3 (the pre-fix `if existing: checkout_room()` would have evicted your first home). **Extra homes are usable, not phantom:** new `engine.housing.resolve_active_home(db, char)` returns the home the player is STANDING IN (`get_housing_for_room` + ownership check), falling back to their most-recent home; the six player home-OPERATION engine fns (`checkout_room`, `housing_store`, `housing_retrieve`, `trophy_mount`, `trophy_unmount`, `sell_home`) and the six `HousingCommand` operation sites now route through it, so storage / trophies / checkout / sell act on the home around you. A single-home owner is unaffected (the fallback is their only home); `revoke_faction_quarters` (faction-admin, not a player op) is left on `get_housing`. New `engine.housing.get_homes(db, char_id)` plural accessor (most-recent first). **Per-planet capping is intentionally NOT enforced** -- `player_housing` carries no planet column to filter on (the old per-planet query was an unfiltered global count); the total cap is the limit. `characters.home_room_id` (the singular recall target) tracks the most-recent purchase; per-home recall is a documented follow-up (`HOUSING.multi_home_recall_target`). New `tests/test_fork_housing_multihome_2026_06_23.py` (5 behavioral, real DB harness: own up to the cap, one-over refused, second buy keeps the first, `resolve_active_home` targets the home you're in / falls back, single-home unaffected). 51 housing tests + 9 housing-tutorial smokes green. Engine + parser + test only; no schema change.

### 2026-06-23 -- FORK: CP.ai_trickle_director_wiring -- `@director trickle` (toggle + knobs + gated award) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Resolves `CP.ai_trickle_director_wiring` (Brian: "wire it and toggle it with a command; start dormant but be able to flip it on; knobs to tune AI spend"). `engine.cp_engine.CPEngine.award_ai_trickle` (the AI-evaluation CP bonus -- clamps to `AI_MAX_TICKS_PER_EVAL=15`, weekly-cap aware, graceful-drop) was fully built but had ZERO callers. **Wired now, default DORMANT:** a module-level runtime toggle `engine.cp_engine.is_cp_ai_trickle_enabled()` / `set_cp_ai_trickle()` (mirrors `engine.narrative._narrative_ai_enabled` -- default off, resets on restart) + a new `@director trickle` admin subcommand (`parser/director_commands.py`): `status` (shows ENABLED/DORMANT + the knob), `enable`/`on` & `disable`/`off` (flip the toggle), and `award <player> [ticks]` (the gated producer -- refuses unless enabled, defaults to the `cp.ai_trickle_ticks` tunable knob, clamps to the per-eval cap, calls `award_ai_trickle`). **Why a discretionary grant, not auto-LLM scoring:** the trigger Brian's call left open (the cult of "what's quality RP") needs an LLM evaluator that doesn't exist and would add a metered cost per eval -- exactly the spend he wants dormant. So the award is a deliberate Director/admin grant (no metered spend, and Guide_26 §7's "no AI grades your prose" claim still holds); auto-LLM-scoring is a documented future flip once enabled. New `tests/test_fork_cp_trickle_2026_06_23.py` (4: the toggle defaults dormant + flips; `@director` dispatches `trickle`; the award is gated on `is_cp_ai_trickle_enabled`, clamped by `AI_MAX_TICKS_PER_EVAL`, and uses the `cp.ai_trickle_ticks` knob). Engine + parser + guide + test only; no schema; no auto faucet (dormant); era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- FORK: SPACE.anomaly_engagement -- per-type `course anomaly <id>` engagement -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Resolves `SPACE.anomaly_engagement_mostly_unwired` (Brian: "we need to fix that" -> Option A, build the real engagement). 6 of 7 space-anomaly types had NO resolution command, yet every full-scan readout instructed the player to type `course anomaly <id>` -- which `CourseCommand` only matched against adjacent ZONES, so it failed ("not an adjacent zone"). Only `derelict` (via `salvage`) was wired. **Fix:** `course anomaly <id>` is now routed (before the pilot-only helm gate, so any crew can engage) to a per-type dispatcher `CourseCommand._engage_anomaly`: it validates the anomaly is fully scanned (`resolution >= scans_needed`), then -- `derelict` -> redirect to `salvage`, `mineral_vein` -> redirect to `mine` (the existing dedicated verbs), and the five previously-dead types resolve through `perform_skill_check` (dice funnel) -> `adjust_credits` (credit funnel) -> `remove_anomaly`: **distress** (Sensors, Easy -- answer the mayday), **cache** (Technical, Moderate -- security bypass; retry on fail), **pirates** (Mechanical/gunnery, Moderate -- scatter the pack), **imperial/Republic dead-drop** (Technical/slicing, Difficult), **mynock** (Mechanical/piloting, Easy -- shake the colony; retry on fail). One-shot types consume the anomaly on a failed attempt; retry types keep it. Rewards are modest (200-2400 cr, crit pays max), gated behind the scan cost + the skill check -- the same faucet class as the existing salvage/mine payouts (era-clean, conservative). New `tests/test_fork_space_anomaly_engage_2026_06_23.py` (6: all 5 types specced + well-formed, derelict/mineral_vein excluded, routing + method wired, the resolution uses the dice/credit/remove funnels, a fully-scanned anomaly meets the gate, and -- importantly -- every engagement skill ACTUALLY rolls a real result). 389 space-suite tests green. **Latent bug discovered (NOT fixed here -- separate, balance-affecting):** every other space command loads its `SkillRegistry` via `sr.load_default()`, but that method does not exist on `engine.character.SkillRegistry` (only `load_file`) -- it raises `AttributeError`, caught by each command's `except` -> `result=None` -> the skill check is silently GRACEFUL-SKIPPED (treated as success). So `scan`/`deepscan`/nav/etc. space skill checks never actually fail in production. My engagement loads correctly via `load_file` (a real gate); fixing the ~6 other sites makes those checks real and is a deliberate follow-up (it makes space harder and may shift tests that assume the always-pass behavior). Parser + test only; no schema; no new faucet class; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- FORK: ENV.hazard_debuff recovery path (drink cure + decay-on-leave) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Resolves the design call `ENV.hazard_debuff_no_cure_path` (Brian: "definitely need recovery" -- Option A, wire a real cure). The desert-heat **dehydration** (-1D STR/-1D DEX at 3 stacks) and **toxic_exposure** (-1D STR) debuffs were `duration_seconds: 0` (permanent) and `engine.buffs.remove_buff()` had ZERO callers, so once a player took these they were stuck with no in-game cure -- the guide had to be reworded to a prevention-only framing. **Recovery (two complementary paths):** (1) Both env debuffs now carry `duration_seconds = 1200` (20 min). Because the hazard tick re-applies the debuff every `HAZARD_CHECK_INTERVAL` (300s) while you're exposed -- and `add_buff` refreshes `started_at` on re-apply -- the debuff PERSISTS while you stand in the heat/toxic air and DECAYS ~20 min after you leave (the natural "breathe clean air / get out of the sun and recover" path; `expire_buffs` prunes it). (2) A new `drink` command (`parser/builtin_commands.py`, aliases `hydrate`): if you carry a `water_canteen` (`engine.hazards._has_mitigation`), drinking clears dehydration INSTANTLY via `remove_buff` and pushes a HUD update; helpful messages cover no-water / not-thirsty. The canteen is durable (no consume), consistent with its existing model. **Balance note:** the only number is the 20-min decay window (> the 5-min hazard re-check, so it never clears while exposed); conservative -- the debuffs still bite while you're in the hazard and recovery has weight. (The hazard difficulty double-scaling -- the other half of this design call -- was fixed in the batch-2-tail drop.) New `tests/test_fork_env_recovery_2026_06_23.py` (5: both durations now > 0; a stale dehydration decays once not refreshed; `remove_buff` clears dehydration; water_canteen detection; the `drink` command is defined + registered). 17 buffs/hazards tests green; `register_all` boots clean with `drink` among 39 commands. Engine + parser + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (batch-2 tail): hazard double-scaling + admin>builder hierarchy + @lore crash -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Three findings closing the breadth-QA batch (wilderness/hazards + director/admin sweeps). **(a) [hazards] Environmental hazard difficulty double-scaled with severity.** `engine/hazards.py` `check_hazard_for_character` read the ALREADY-severity-scaled stored difficulty (`set_room_hazard` / `_check_wilderness_hazard` bake in `base + (severity-1)*3`) and then added `(severity-1)*3` AGAIN -- a severity-3 hazard hit DC 22 (DC 25 with the daytime modifier) instead of the intended 16. Fix: use the stored value as-is; apply the one-time severity scaling only to the defensive raw-base fallback. (This is the secondary finding flagged with the ENV.hazard_debuff fork; the recovery-path half of that fork is still queued.) **(b) [admin, CORRUPTION] ADMIN > BUILDER privilege hierarchy was not enforced.** `parser/commands.py` `check_access` for `AccessLevel.BUILDER` checked only `is_builder`, so an account with `is_admin=1, is_builder=0` (exactly the state `@grant <char> = admin` produces) was denied EVERY builder tool (`@teleport`/`@set`/`@destroy`/`@spawn`/`@name`/`@lock`/`@zone`/...). Fix: the BUILDER gate now passes for `is_builder` OR `is_admin` -- an admin implicitly inherits builder. (`test_t321_admin_audit.test_builder_command_uses_builder_flag` set is_admin too -- it now explicitly clears both flags so it still tests a pure non-privileged denial.) **(c) [admin, CRASH] `@lore add priority=<non-number>` threw an unhandled `ValueError`** (`parser/director_commands.py`), surfacing the generic "An error occurred" to the admin with no clue. Fix: a `try/except (ValueError, TypeError)` parses the priority first and returns a clean "Priority must be a number (1-10)." The director/admin sweep otherwise verified all 18 authorization gates correct (no privilege-escalation bypass), the `@director cult` state machine, `@economy` throttle clamping, and `@force` (forced commands stay subject to the target's own access check) all clean. New `tests/test_qa_batch2_tail_2026_06_23.py` (3 structural guards). 40+ hazards/admin-audit tests green. Engine + parser + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink; era-clean. **Breadth-QA campaign COMPLETE** -- 13 clusters swept across 2 rounds + breadth; mail/comms was the only fully-clean cluster.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (achievements): +achievements dead for everyone (BLOCKER) + popular_figure unreachable -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Two SWALLOW findings from the achievements/progression sweep. **#1 [BLOCKER] `+achievements` was dead for EVERY player** -- `parser/achievement_commands.py` resolved its DB handle as `ctx.session.game_server.db if hasattr(ctx.session, "game_server") else None`, but `Session` has no `game_server` attribute (nothing sets it), so `hasattr` was always False, `db` was always None, and the command always printed "Achievement system unavailable." -- the entire achievement display surface was unreachable. Fix: use the already-wired `ctx.db` (the handle every other command uses) -- one line. **#2 [SWALLOW] the `popular_figure` achievement (threshold 10 kudos) was permanently unreachable** -- `parser/cp_commands.py` passed `on_kudos_received` the WEEKLY kudos count (`kudos_count_received_this_week`, capped at `KUDOS_PER_WEEK=3`), so the progress counter could never reach 10, contradicting the hook's own "Pass lifetime total" contract. Fix: a new `db.kudos_count_received_lifetime(target_id)` (counts all `kudos_log` rows for the target, mirroring the weekly method) is now passed instead. New `tests/test_qa_achievements_2026_06_23.py` (4: the `db = ctx.db` wiring + the buggy assignment is gone; cp_commands passes the lifetime count + the weekly call is gone from that block; the db method exists; a BEHAVIORAL lifetime-vs-weekly count test that seeds an old + a fresh kudos and asserts weekly==1 / lifetime==2). 154 achievement/cp/kudos tests green. Engine/parser/db + test only; new db method is additive; no schema change; achievement CP reward still rides its funnel; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (wilderness): Tatooine anomaly system silently dead (slug mismatch, BLOCKER-class) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
[SWALLOW, BLOCKER-class] The ENTIRE Tatooine wilderness anomaly system (Tier 1/2/3) was silently dead. The anomaly templates in `engine/wilderness_anomalies.py` tagged the bare region slug `dune_sea`, but the wilderness YAML (`data/worlds/clone_wars/wilderness/dune_sea.yaml`) declares `slug: tatooine_dune_sea`, so rooms carry `wilderness_region_id = "tatooine_dune_sea"`. The spawn tick enumerates regions via `SELECT DISTINCT wilderness_region_id FROM rooms` and calls `spawn_anomaly_for_region(db, "tatooine_dune_sea", ...)`, so `_pick_template(region_slug="tatooine_dune_sea")` matched NONE of the 5 Tier-1 / 3 Tier-2 / 1 Tier-3 Tatooine templates -- `anomalies` always showed "No active anomalies" in the Tatooine wilderness, forever. (`coruscant_underworld` worked because its templates match its own full slug.) **Fix:** the Tatooine templates now tag the full DB slug `tatooine_dune_sea` (matching the `<planet>_<region>` convention coruscant_underworld already follows) -- 10 occurrences. Changing the YAML slug instead would violate the additive-only world-data invariant and orphan the DB data. The 3 SYN.7a/7b/8 unit suites (which seeded a self-consistent `dune_sea` world and so pinned the same wrong slug) were slug-updated to `tatooine_dune_sea` (94 references, lookbehind-safe). New `tests/test_qa_wilderness_anomaly_slug_2026_06_23.py` (4: `_pick_template` now matches the full Tatooine slug at T1+T2, the bare `dune_sea` slug is gone, coruscant_underworld still matches). 153 wilderness-anomaly tests green. ### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (bounty): offline-hunter credit loss + phantom alive-bonus + cancel-swallows-escrow -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Three findings from the bounty-lifecycle break-it sweep. **#1 [CORRUPTION] NPC bounty reward lost when the hunter was OFFLINE at the target's bleed-out death.** The auto-collect kill hook (`parser/combat_commands.py`) trapped the only `adjust_credits` inside an `if _sess and _sess.character:` guard, but `notify_target_killed` had already marked the contract COLLECTED + deleted the NPC (irreversible) -- so an offline hunter who mortally wounded the target and logged off before the bleed-out got NOTHING. Fix: award the credits UNCONDITIONALLY (the DB write needs no session); only the in-game "[BOUNTY COLLECTED]" message stays gated on an online session. **#2 [SWALLOW] `reward_alive_bonus` advertised on the board but never paid** -- every `collect` / `total_reward` call hardcoded `alive=False`, so the alive bonus the board displayed was a phantom faucet. Fix: the manual `+bounty/collect` (`parser/bounty_commands.py`) now detects a CAPTURED-alive target (`wound_level == 5`, mortally wounded/incapacitated but not DEAD vs `== 6` killed/deleted) and passes `alive=captured_alive` to both `collect` and `total_reward`, so capturing a target alive and turning them in actually pays base + alive bonus. **#3 [SWALLOW] `+pcbounty cancel` with a corrupt/empty `contributors_json` silently refunded $0** (`parser/pc_bounty_commands.py`) -- a JSON parse failure set `contributors=[]`, `_proportional_refunds([], pool)` returned `[]`, the refund loop never ran, the bounty was marked canceled, and the entire escrow vanished with no error. Fix: a fallback refunds the whole pool to the poster who is canceling when the contributors record is corrupt/empty. New `tests/test_qa_bounty_2026_06_23.py` (5: the unconditional-award ordering, the captured-alive wiring + the dead hardcoded-False is gone, the cancel fallback + `_proportional_refunds` single-poster math). 117 bounty/pc-bounty tests green. Parser + test only; no schema; bounty payout still rides the `adjust_credits` funnel; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (Force): victim session cache not synced after injure_kill / telekinesis-disarm -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Two CORRUPTION findings from the Force-powers-in-use sweep. A Force power lands from the ATTACKER's command, so the TARGET's session cache was never updated -- the victim's HUD/sheet kept showing them HEALTHY (after `force injure_kill`) or still-armed (after `force telekinesis` disarm) until the victim's NEXT command refreshed the session from the DB. The live combat object was always correct; only the victim's display lagged for that window. **#1 `_save_target_after_force`** (`parser/force_commands.py`) saved `wound_level` to the DB but never synced the target's session dict or pushed their HUD. **#2 `_apply_disarm`** wrote the cleared equipment to the DB and already had the target session in hand (it sent them a notify line) but never updated its cached `equipment`. Fix: both now `find_by_character(target_id)` and, if the victim is online, sync the cached state (`wound_level`; or `equipment` + clearing the legacy `equipped_weapon` bare key) and `send_hud_update(...)` after the DB write -- so the victim's display reflects the hit immediately. New `tests/test_qa_force_session_sync_2026_06_23.py` (2 structural guards that each function syncs the target session + HUD after its save). 363 Force-suite tests green. Parser + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink; DSP ratchet + `force_sensitive` derivation untouched.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (housing): checkout_room FK crash (BLOCKER) + guest-list always-False -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Two fixes from the housing break-it sweep. **#1 [CRASH+CORRUPTION, BLOCKER] `checkout_room` crashed on EVERY vacate path.** It deleted `rooms` then `player_housing` BEFORE clearing the FK cross-references (`characters.home_room_id -> rooms.id`, `rooms.housing_id -> player_housing.id`), so the room DELETE failed silently and the `player_housing` DELETE then crashed UNCAUGHT (`FOREIGN KEY constraint failed`) -- and the deposit refund had already fired, injecting credits with no state cleanup. Blast radius: `housing checkout`, `housing sell` (Tier 3 via `sell_home`), `@housing evict`, faction-quarter revoke, and the weekly rent-eviction tick -- all broken. Fix: `checkout_room` now NULL-clears `characters.home_room_id` (for any char pointing at the rooms) and `rooms.housing_id` BEFORE the deletes, mirroring the already-correct `sell_shopfront` ordering. **#2 [CORRUPTION] `is_on_guest_list` always returned False** -- it did `char_id in guests` where `guests` is a list of `{"id","name"}` dicts (an int is never `in` a list of dicts), so invited guests were permanently locked out of a private home. Fix: `any(isinstance(g, dict) and g.get("id") == char_id for g in guests)`. New `tests/test_qa_housing_checkout_guest_2026_06_23.py` (7: guest-list membership across member/non-member/empty; a BEHAVIORAL rent->checkout that genuinely reproduces the FK crash on unfixed code, the harness DB running `PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON`, asserting clean vacate + record-gone + `home_room_id` cleared; + a structural guard that the FK clears precede the deletes). 17 housing tests green. Engine + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink change (the deposit refund already rides the credit funnel); era-clean. **Deferred (economy-touching design question, logged for Brian):** the sweep also found `MAX_TIER3_TOTAL=4`/`MAX_TIER3_PER_PLANET=1` are dead code -- `purchase_home` blocks ANY 2nd Tier-3 home globally instead of enforcing the per-planet/total caps. Wiring the constants would enable up to 4 homes (1/planet); since it loosens the economy I left it for a Brian intent-confirmation rather than guess.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (ships/space): salvage crash (BLOCKER) + disembark crew-slot leak + sell-cargo atomicity -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Three findings from the ships/space-combat break-it sweep. **#1 [CRASH+CORRUPTION, BLOCKER] `salvage`/`mine`/`harvest` crashed on the bridge broadcast.** All three called `ctx.session_mgr.broadcast_to_room(..., exclude_session=ctx.session)`, but the signature is `broadcast_to_room(room_id, text, exclude=None, source_char=None)` (`server/session.py:2307`) -- the wrong kwarg raised `TypeError` BEFORE `remove_anomaly(...)`, so a successful salvage surfaced "An error occurred" to the player AND left the wreck infinitely farmable (the only wired anomaly engagement, broken). Fix: `exclude_session=` -> `exclude=` at all three sites (`parser/space_commands.py`). **#2 [CORRUPTION] `disembark` cleared only the pilot seat + gunner stations.** A disembarking copilot/engineer/navigator/commander/sensors left their seat stuck-occupied (no one could take it), and a cleared slot surfaced a stale "#None" to the next claimant. Fix: `DisembarkCommand.execute` now loops over `_SINGLE_STATIONS` (pilot/copilot/engineer/navigator/commander/sensors), clearing every seat the player holds. **#3 [CORRUPTION] `sell cargo` removed the cargo before crediting the player** (`update_ship(cargo=...)` then an unchecked `adjust_credits`), so a failed credit write left the cargo gone with no payment. Fix: `_handle_sell_cargo` now credits FIRST (confirms a non-None return) and removes the cargo only after -- mirroring the buy path's credits-before-goods ordering; the failure mode is now player-favorable (paid, cargo kept) rather than player-harmful. New `tests/test_qa_space_salvage_disembark_2026_06_23.py` (5: a `broadcast_to_room` signature contract that makes the wrong-kwarg class unrepresentable + a no-`exclude_session`-anywhere guard; the disembark all-stations loop; the `_SINGLE_STATIONS` coverage; the sell-cargo credit-first ordering + None-check). 21 prior space-breakit + the 5 new tests green. Parser + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink change (credits still ride `adjust_credits`); era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- NPE fix: standalone chargen wizard couldn't load tutorial chains (HTTP 401) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Found by the new Playwright E2E harness: the STANDALONE `/chargen` wizard (the portal's 'Create Character' link) showed *'Failed to load chains (HTTP 401)'* at the CHAIN step, so a new player entering that way couldn't pick a tutorial chain (NEXT stayed enabled, so they proceeded into the game with NO onboarding chain). `handle_chains` (`server/api.py`) required a valid account token, but the standalone first-character flow has none (the token is only issued AFTER account creation; `loadChains()` reads `EMBED_TOKEN`, set only in the EMBEDDED `/chargen?embedded=1&token=` flow). **Fix:** a TOKENLESS `/api/chargen/chains` request is now served as the FIRST-character picker (`is_first_character=True`, `existing_chars=[]`) -- the chain list is public chargen content built from the `__chargen_any__` sentinel, not account data, so no auth is needed to display it. A SUPPLIED-but-invalid/expired token (the embedded alt-creation flow) is still rejected 401, and a valid token still computes `is_first_character` from the account. Updated `tests/test_drop2b_chargen_chains_endpoint_and_consumer.py` (`test_missing_token_rejected` -> `test_missing_token_serves_first_character_picker`: tokenless now 200 + `is_first_character` + non-empty chains; bad-token stays 401); 37 chargen tests green. **Validated end-to-end** by re-running the E2E harness: the chain step now renders the real picker (Republic Soldier / Republic Intelligence / Jedi Path / Separatist chains) instead of the 401 error. Server + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 -- QA break-it (combat exit): co-op kill stranded players (BLOCKER) + walking out orphaned combat (CORRUPTION) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Two round-2 break-it findings, both about leaving combat. **BLOCKER (combat sweep): a CO-OP PvE kill stranded both players** -- the core mob-grind loop. `engine/combat.py` `CombatInstance.is_over` only counts heads (`len(active_combatants) <= 1`), so when 2+ allied PCs drop the last NPC, `active_combatants` is still `[PC, PC]` -> `is_over` is False forever: `disengage` refused ("Combat is still active") and `flee` resolved an opposed roll vs an ALLY. Both players were stuck -- couldn't trade, shop, heal, or leave. **CORRUPTION (movement sweep): `MoveCommand` had no in-combat gate** (`parser/builtin_commands.py`), so a player could walk a normal exit out of an active fight, orphaning the `CombatInstance` in `_active_combats` (NPCs left in a zombie combat, `who` showing stale 'In Combat', a slow leak). Both violate the system's own intent -- `flee` is the designed combat exit (disengage literally says "use flee"). **Fix:** a PvP-aware parser-level predicate `parser/combat_commands._combat_finished(combat)` -- the fight is over unless two MUTUALLY HOSTILE combatants can both still act (NPCs are hostile to every PC; two PCs are hostile only under a live `_pvp_active` pact, TTL-checked). It differs from `is_over` ONLY in the co-op case (2+ allied PCs, no NPCs, no PvP), so PvP and 1v1 are untouched. It now backs the round-resolution end-check (player + admin paths), so a co-op kill AUTO-ENDS the combat (combat_ended broadcast + `_remove_combat` cleanup the round the NPC dies), and `disengage`. `MoveCommand.execute` now refuses to walk out of an unfinished combat the char is in (-> "Use `flee` to attempt escape"), covering both ground and wilderness moves; the check is fail-open (a FINISHED leftover combat does not pin). New `tests/test_qa_combat_exit_2026_06_23.py` (10: the predicate across empty/lone/NPC-vs-PC/co-op-allied/only-NPCs/live-PvP/expired-PvP/PvP-among-allies + structural guards that no `is_over` decision sites remain and the move gate is wired). 464 combat + movement regression tests green. Parser + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink; era-clean.

### 2026-06-22 -- Web-client E2E test harness (Playwright PoC): the new-player flow, automated in a real browser -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Closes the one QA axis the in-process break-it sweeps and the jsdom unit tests structurally can't reach: the ACTUAL rendered web SPA in a real browser (clicks, the WebSocket round-trip, rendering) -- the web-first launch surface. New `tests/e2e/playwright_new_player_poc.py` (+ `tests/e2e/README.md`): boots `main.py` on a free port + a throwaway temp DB (schema + world auto-create on boot; `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` cleared so the Director never spends), launches headless Chromium (Google-fonts aborted so offline can't hang it), and drives the WHOLE new-player flow -- portal -> the real chargen wizard (state-machine on the active `.step-panel`, so the template's species-skip is handled) -> account submit -> the client login form -> character select -> live game (first `hud_update`) -> a `look` command -> a click on the always-visible mini-map exit strip (`#g-map-exits`) -- screenshotting every screen to `tests/e2e/_screens/` (gitignored) for vision review. The PoC PASSES end to end and the exit-strip click moved the character Landing Pad -> Desert Trail, validating the click-to-move fix in a real browser (not just jsdom). Local + headless, no API cost. **Box note:** the one-time `playwright install chromium chromium-headless-shell` hit Norton's TLS-scanning CA (`UNABLE_TO_VERIFY_LEAF_SIGNATURE`); fixed by making Playwright's bundled Node read the Windows cert store via `NODE_OPTIONS=--use-system-ca` (the Node analogue of the Python `truststore` fix; see the `anthropic-api-box-blockers` memory). **Finding surfaced by the PoC (NPE):** the STANDALONE `/chargen` wizard (the portal's 'Create Character' link) renders *'Failed to load chains (HTTP 401)'* at the CHAIN step -- `loadChains()` fetches `/api/chargen/chains?token=<EMBED_TOKEN>` but `EMBED_TOKEN` is only set in EMBEDDED mode (`/chargen?embedded=1&token=`), so the standalone first-character flow has no token and `handle_chains` (`server/api.py:702`) returns 401. A new player entering via the portal link can't pick a tutorial chain (NEXT is still enabled, so they proceed without one). Logged for a fix (tokenless first-character chain list). Tooling + docs only; no engine/schema/faucet/sink change.

### 2026-06-22 -- QA break-it (faction): 2nd region contest silently couldn't transfer ownership (UNIQUE trap, BLOCKER) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
The faction/territory break-it sweep found a BLOCKER-class state corruption in the region-contest endgame. `region_contests` carries `UNIQUE(region_slug, status)` (`engine/contest.py:216`) -- intended to keep ONE ACTIVE contest per region, but it ALSO forbids a second *resolved* row of the same status. Resolved rows are never deleted (cooldowns live in their own `region_contest_cooldowns` table), so once a region had a `resolved_challenger` (or `resolved_defender`) row, the next same-outcome resolution's `UPDATE region_contests SET status='resolved_challenger' WHERE id=? AND status='active'` collided with the leftover row, raised `IntegrityError`, and was swallowed by the resolution path's `try/except` (`engine/contest.py` `_resolve_challenger_win` ~1608 / `_resolve_defender_win` ~876): the function returned early, so **ownership never transferred, no cooldown/anchor-despawn/notification** -- and EVERY future contest on that region was permanently broken. Reachable in normal play on any region after one full contest cycle; also already latent in any live DB (`SELECT region_slug,status FROM region_contests WHERE status!='active'` -- any row there = that region's next contest is broken). **Fix:** both resolution paths now `DELETE` the prior same-status resolved row for the region (`... AND id != ?`, so the current contest and the concurrent-double-resolve CAS are unaffected) immediately before the resolving `UPDATE`. Resolved rows are stale history, so this is safe; it also **self-heals** an already-stuck region on its next resolution. The legitimate intent of the constraint (one ACTIVE contest per region) is preserved. New `tests/test_qa_contest_second_resolution_2026_06_22.py` (6: real-schema proof that the bare UPDATE collides on a 2nd same-status resolve while DELETE-then-UPDATE resolves three successive challenger- AND defender-wins cleanly, one-active-per-region still enforced, + structural guards that both paths DELETE before the UPDATE). Updated `tests/test_contest_anchor_lifecycle.py` (the two CAS-skip tests asserted exactly 1 statement before the no-op-CAS bail; the legitimate pre-UPDATE DELETE makes it 2 -- the bail-without-follow-up intent is unchanged). 206 contest-suite tests green. Engine + test only; no schema migration (constraint kept, stale rows cleared at resolve); influence funnel untouched; era-clean.

### 2026-06-22 -- QA break-it (crafting): outdoor survey quality band + teach gate bypass (2 MEDIUM) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
The crafting/gathering break-it sweep found two MEDIUM defects, both confirmed at HEAD. **#1 [CORRUPTION] outdoor survey used the city quality band.** The `survey` command (`parser/crafting_commands.py`) classifies the room by name to pick resource TYPES (`get_survey_resources` via `_OUTDOOR_ZONE_KEYWORDS`: outdoor zones yield metal/organic) but called `survey_quality_from_margin(result.margin)` WITHOUT `is_outdoor`, so the quality band was always the city 30-60 instead of the designed outdoor 60-90 (per the function's own docstring). Outdoor harvesting (Jundland/Dune Sea/desert/mesa/plains) silently yielded systematically lower quality -- and since survey amount scales with quality, fewer resources too. **Fix:** a new single-source `engine.crafting.is_outdoor_zone(zone_name)` now drives BOTH the type selection (`get_survey_resources`) and the quality band, and the command passes `is_outdoor=is_outdoor_zone(room_name)`. **NOTE (balance):** this roughly doubles outdoor survey quality (30-60 -> 60-90) -- it restores the documented design intent that was never wired, not a new tuning choice; flag for an economist glance if the resource economy is sensitive. **#2 [SWALLOW] `teach` bypassed the T5 questline/rep gate.** `LearnCommand` checks `_schematic_gate_met` before `add_known_schematic`, but `TeachCommand` did not -- so a player who had earned a gated T5 master recipe could teach it to anyone, who could then craft it (`can_craft` checks resources only, not gates). **Fix:** `TeachCommand` now checks `_schematic_gate_met(target_char, schematic, ctx.db)` and refuses to teach a gated recipe to a target who hasn't cleared the questline + faction-rep gate; an ungated schematic always passes, so ordinary teaching is unaffected. New `tests/test_qa_crafting_survey_teach_gate_2026_06_22.py` (9: is_outdoor_zone classification, the two quality bands, outdoor>city at equal margin, the survey-command wiring guard; `_schematic_gate_met` ungated-pass + questline-gated-block, and a structural guard that the teach gate precedes `add_known_schematic`). 431 crafting/survey/harvest regression tests green. Engine + parser + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink (resources are crafting mats, not credits); era-clean.

### 2026-06-22 -- QA break-it (economy): vendor-droid unstock/buy wiped a bare-list inventory (2 BLOCKERs) -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
The economy break-it sweep found two BLOCKER item-integrity bugs in `engine/vendor_droids.py`, siblings of the QA-M3 bare-list class. The `characters.inventory` schema default is a bare JSON list `"[]"` (carried by every fresh char and any char that only ever held general items); the crafting/`add_to_inventory` helpers instead persist the dict shape `{"items":[...],"resources":[...]}`. The M3 fix (2026-06-17) routed `stock_droid` / `_find_in_inventory` through `engine.items.coerce_inventory` (normalizes any shape, preserving items) but MISSED `unstock_droid` (L484) and `buy_from_droid` (L771): both parsed the inventory inline as `json.loads(...)` then `if not isinstance(_, dict): _ = {}` -- which silently WIPES a bare list to an empty dict before appending the single returned/bought item. **Effect:** a player with a bare-list inventory who unstocks an item from their own vendor droid, or buys an item from another player's droid, loses EVERY other item they were carrying (the operation reports success). **Fix:** both now use `coerce_inventory(char.get("inventory", "[]"))`, matching `stock_droid` -- the bare list is preserved as `items` and only the returned/bought item is appended. New `tests/test_qa_vendor_unstock_buy_bare_list_2026_06_22.py` (5: drive the REAL `unstock_droid`/`buy_from_droid` with a faked DB and assert pre-existing bare-list items survive a bare list, an empty `"[]"` default, and dict-form; `buy` patches `apply_city_tax` inert). 82 vendor/shop regression tests green (incl. the M3 suite). Engine fix + test only; no schema; no faucet/sink (credit legs already ride `adjust_credits`); era-clean. **Also from the sweep -- mail/comms/social was clean of blockers** (verified mail access-control, XSS escaping, party flows safe); 2 LOW storage-DoS gaps logged for a hardening batch: no server-side length cap on the mail `subject` (`parser/mail_commands.py` `_do_send`) or the `+finger/set` fields (`parser/mux_commands.py` `_set_field`), unlike the body (8k cap) and `+rpprefs` notes (120 cap).

### 2026-06-22 -- Map click-to-move: always-every-exit strip on the always-visible mini-map -- *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
**Live bug (Brian):** on the always-visible mini-map only SOME exits were clickable (e.g. "Docking Bay 94 - Entrance" offered only `down`, not `north`/`northwest`). **Root cause:** on-map click-to-walk (`_decorateMiniForClickToWalk`) only tags rooms that render a `<g data-room-id>` marker, but `L_SubstrateRooms` (`static/spa/m3_composition_engine.js`) skips `street`/`hub`-style rooms -- so an exit whose destination is a street/hub had NO clickable target; and the qa-row direction chips (`rebuildDirectionButtons`) cap at the first 4 exits, so >4-exit rooms dropped some. The sector-map MODAL already solved this with an always-every-exit button strip from `lastExits` (`_renderModalExitStrip`); the always-visible mini did not. **Fix (kills the class, not one room):** extracted a shared `_buildExitStrip(strip, afterClick)` that builds one always-clickable button per current-room exit from the authoritative `lastExits` (`[{dir,label}]`, set on every look/move) -- UNCAPPED, so >4-exit rooms render all exits and the flex row wraps. `_renderModalExitStrip` now delegates to it (with a modal-close afterClick); a new `_renderMiniExitStrip` mounts the same strip on the always-visible mini-map (new `#g-map-exits` container under the map, `.map-exits` CSS) with no afterClick. The mini strip is refreshed on every room change at both `rebuildDirectionButtons` call sites (exits-present + no-exits). Every exit is now clickable regardless of which rooms draw markers or how many exits a room has. **Files:** `static/client.html` (shared builder + mini renderer + HTML container + CSS + 2 refresh call sites; `window._sw_renderMiniExitStrip` exported). New `tests/spa/test_minimap_exit_strip.py` (4 tests, jsdom, runs the REAL functions extracted from client.html: all exits incl a markerless street become clickable + route to `sendCmd`; a 6-exit room renders all 6 uncapped; empty exits clear the strip; the modal strip regression-passes incl its close-on-click). Regression: `test_clickwalk_slugjoin.py` + `test_client_onclick_exports.py` green (11). Client only; no engine/schema/faucet/sink change; era-clean.

### 2026-06-23 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: player-housing economy + checkout-teardown FK fix — *drop t319-housing-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The player-housing economy (`engine/housing.py`) moved credits via `adjust_credits` (tags `housing_purchase` / `housing_rent` / `housing_deposit_refund` / `home_prestige`) but those isolated `credit_flow` rows can't be rejoined offline into the housing **lifecycle** — the acquire → weekly-rent → overdue → forfeit funnel, voluntary-checkout churn, or the deposit-forfeit rate — the direct signal for tuning `TIER1_WEEKLY_RENT` / `TIER1_DEPOSIT` / `TIER1_EVICT_WEEKS`. This drop adds ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `housing` event (new module helper `_emit_housing`) at every credit-moving transition: **acquire** (`rent_room`, the deposit+first-week sink, with deposit/weekly_rent/lot_id), **rent_paid** (`tick_housing_rent`, the weekly-rent sink), **rent_overdue** (the tick that couldn't collect — `amount=0` + `weeks_overdue`), **checkout** (`checkout_room`, the deposit-refund faucet + a `forfeited` flag), and **prestige** (`purchase_home_prestige`, the cosmetic-tier sink). Each carries a coerced `char_id` + the signed `amount` so the offline funnel joins per-player. Buffer-only + offline-flushed → zero gameplay behaviour; every emit is wrapped fail-open so a broken sink can never disturb the rent/acquire/checkout it observes. Sampling honours `telemetry.housing_sample` (default 1.0; documented in `data/tunables.yaml`). The checkout emit is placed right after the committed deposit refund (before the room teardown) so the economic signal survives a teardown hiccup. **BUG FIX surfaced by the new suite (no test had ever driven `checkout_room`):** `checkout_room` nulled `characters.home_room_id` AFTER deleting the housing room, but `home_room_id` is an FK to `rooms(id)` (set by `rent_room`) — so under `PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON` (production posture) the room delete FK-failed, the room survived FK-pinned, and the unwrapped `DELETE FROM player_housing` then crashed on the `rooms.housing_id` FK = a **checkout/eviction crash** (a player vacating a room, or the rent tick evicting one, would raise). Fixed by clearing `home_room_id` BEFORE the teardown and migrating the manual two-tracked-exit delete + raw room `DELETE` to the canonical FK-safe `delete_room` (mirrors the sibling `sell_shopfront` fix, 2026-06-21). No schema change, era-clean, funnel-routed (no new credit movement). 22 tests (`tests/test_t319_housing_telemetry.py`): the five transition emits driven end-to-end against the harness DB (acquire/rent_paid/overdue/checkout/prestige), refused-overdraw emits nothing, ledger-leg cross-check, `telemetry.housing_sample` honoured, fail-open under a raising sink, the helper field schema + id coercion, the seam source-pins, and a **checkout-teardown FK-safe regression** (full teardown completes, rooms + housing record gone, no crash).

### 2026-06-23 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: tutorial-chain onboarding-economy funnel — *drop t319-chain-reward-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The tutorial-chain reward pipeline (`engine/chain_rewards.py`) moved credits via `adjust_credits` (tags `chain_step_reward` / `chain_reward`) but those ledger rows can't be rejoined offline into an onboarding funnel — no chain identity, no item/rep breadth, and crucially **no signal at all for a graduation that awards zero credits** (a chain *completion* is the load-bearing NPE health metric). This drop adds ONE fail-open `chain_reward` telemetry event at the two delivery seams, mirroring the established `objective` funnel (single event type, `phase` tags the lifecycle transition): `apply_step_rewards` emits `phase="step"` **only when a reward was actually delivered** (most steps carry `reward: {}` — empty steps emit nothing, no spam), `apply_graduation_rewards` **always** emits `phase="graduation"` (the completion event is the signal even at 0 credits). Fields capture chain_id/step + the reward profile (credits, item count, rep-faction count, achievement count, error count) and a coerced `char_id` so the offline funnel can compute count(step) vs count(graduation) per chain + the credit/item flow the onboarding pipeline injects. Buffer-only + offline-flushed → zero gameplay behaviour; both emits are wrapped fail-open so a broken sink can never disturb the reward delivery it observes. No schema change, era-clean, funnel-routed (no new credit movement). 11 tests (`tests/test_t319_chain_reward_telemetry.py`).

### 2026-06-23 — GUIDES authoritative quality pass: Guide_19 Medical & Death (the last unguarded player guide) — *drop guide-19-medical-death-authoritative* (Opus loop)
**Authoritative Opus quality pass** over `data/guides/Guide_19_Medical_Death.md` (v1.0 → v1.1) — the final player guide to receive an authoritative pass (every other guide is now guarded). The earlier Sonnet draft (`guide-19-medical-death-rework`) added the gear-insurance section; this pass reconciled every command, syntax, and mechanical number against HEAD (`parser/medical_commands.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py` Respawn/Loot/Bacta, `parser/insurance_commands.py`, `engine/death.py`, `engine/gear_insurance.py`, `engine/buffs.py`, `engine/character.py`, `engine/force_powers.py`, `engine/hazards.py`) and corrected a dense layer of test-invisible defects: (1) **Respawn is a MANUAL command** (`respawn`/`revive`), not automatic — `on_pc_death` only drops the corpse + sets `wound_state`; the player must `respawn` to return — **and it always lands at a fixed room** (`DEFAULT_RESPAWN_ROOM_ID = 1`, the Mos Eisley landing-pad med bay), so the guide's "nearest cantina / BHG chapter house / closest town" claims and the Scenario-4 "Coruscant central hub" respawn were phantom; rewrote §4 steps 7-8, "The respawn", and Scenarios 3/4. (2) **Loot syntax was wrong** — the guide showed `loot <item> from corpse` / `loot all from corpse` + a `look corpse` examine; real syntax is `loot <name>` (everything) / `loot <name> <item>` keyed by the dead owner's **name**, and there is **no corpse-examine command** (corpses show only in the room `look` listing). Fixed §4 + the §8 quick-ref. (3) **"You never lose credits on death" was unqualified** — a bountied PC killed by a Bounty Hunters' Guild member eats a `bh_insurance_hit` (`INSURANCE_FLAT` 250 + `INSURANCE_PCT` 10% of the bounty; shortfall → insurance debt); added the §4.5 caveat + §9 row. (4) **Stim effects were wrong** — adrenaline shot is **+2D** Strength (`adrenaline_shot` `strength: 6`), not "+1D, sustained", and **all stims are 5-minute timed buffs** (`duration_seconds: 300`), not "one roll"; fixed the §3 effect table (added a Duration column) + §9. (5) **Undocumented healing/medic depth added**: the **medpac family** (`stim <player> with medpac`/`_advanced`/`_fastflesh` — heals 1/2/1 wound levels at First Aid 10/11/8, a no-credit alternative to paid `heal`), the **`stim/force` overdose path** (+5 difficulty; a failed overdose incapacitates), **self-stim −1D** (stimpack/focus/medpac only; adrenaline/combat can't be self-administered), the **one-active-stim** rule, the medic-must-hold-the-stim consumption rule, and the heal **critical (2 levels) / near-miss (no charge)** outcomes. (6) `+medical` relabelled from a phantom "dashboard/status" to the verb umbrella it is; `+sheet` corrected to "shows the wound-LEVEL Condition line" (it renders no `wound_state` countdown — §10 pitfall #3 reframed). (7) **Anti-grief documented**: repeat-kill corpse-loot decay (`GRIEF_LOOT_FACTORS` 1.0/0.5/0.25/0.0 within `GRIEF_WINDOW_SECONDS` 30 min) + the 60-second PvP respawn grace (`RESPAWN_GRACE_SECONDS`). (8) §6 fixed — Accelerate Healing is **self-only** (`target="self"`), so the Force-medic build is self-sufficiency, not Force-healing others; added the stun-KO rule (simultaneous stuns ≥ STR dice → unconscious) to §1. New `tests/test_guide_19_medical_death_authoritative.py` (25 tests) pins the heal/stim/medpac difficulties, the +2D adrenaline magnitude + 300s durations, bacta (500)/pack (150)/insurance (500)/bounty-hit (250+10%) prices, the 1h wound-recovery + 2h/4h decay windows, the fixed respawn room, anti-grief/grace constants, the WoundLevel penalty dice, the 300s hazard interval, the self-only Force heal, every documented command key, and guards all eight corrected phantoms from returning; the earlier draft guard (`test_guide_19_medical_death_rework.py`) still passes unchanged. Docs + test only; engine + data READ-ONLY (death.py/combat.py untouched — avoid-lane respected); era-clean; no schema; no faucet/sink.

Fixed both: Scenario 2 now pays the crit at the full **+200 cr** (net **+360 cr** across the streak, recomputed) and §11 reads **Bet × 1.0 — house waives its 10% cut**. **AUDIENCE BONUS is success-only (§4).** The guide claimed the +15%/head (cap +60%) audience multiplier "applies to successes and partials" — but the engine applies `audience_multiplier()` only inside the success branch; a partial pays a flat `_PARTIAL_PAY * brawl_mult` with no audience lift. Rewrote to "any performance that lands as a success — ordinary or critical — but **not** a near-miss partial." **AURA ENDS EARLY ON PERFORMER DEPARTURE (§5).** The guide framed the 30-min aura as purely timer-bound ("walking out ends *your* exposure"); the move hook in `builtin_commands.py` clears the aura the moment the **performer** leaves the room (`clear_morale_aura` gated on `performer_id == char_id`). Added the early-clear + noted the `look` room-surface flavor line. **PERFORM PAY EXAMPLE (§4):** the "roll of 12 vs 10 → 50 cr" example understated the real `margin/10` linear scale (margin 2 ≈ 80 cr); rewrote to the accurate floor-at-difficulty / ceiling-at-margin-10 framing with the midpoint (~125 cr at margin 5). **`[CRITICAL]` TAG CLARIFIED (§3):** added a note that the tag marks the exploding wild die and only *pays* as a crit if the roll also beats the dealer — a wild explosion that falls short is an ordinary loss (the engine still prints `[CRITICAL]` on that roll line). **Quick-ref (§10):** documented the real aliases (`sabacc` → `gamble`/`cards`; `perform` → `entertain`/`play`). Guard test `tests/test_guide_23_sabacc_entertainer.py` updated: the stale `test_guide_states_crit_is_recognition_only` (which *required* "same as a win") replaced by `test_guide_states_crit_waives_house_cut` (asserts the stale claims are gone + the cut-waive is present); added `test_audience_bonus_is_success_only_not_partial` and `test_aura_clears_when_performer_leaves_room`; docstring crit bullet corrected. 18 tests green.
