### 2026-06-22 — Force-sensitive chargen BLOCKER + cluster (WEG 1D starting rule) — *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Three producer bugs confirmed by the design call FORCE.chargen_sensitivity_representation (resolved to "1D starting"). **(a) [BLOCKER] `server/api.py` `handle_submit` + `handle_create_character`** both wrote `DicePool(0,0)` for a force-sensitive char's control/sense/alter — `from_db_dict` correctly rejects 0D (the L2 fix, pool.is_zero()), so the chargen character was marked non-Force-sensitive after the first DB round-trip and `list_powers_for_char` returned empty. Fixed: both producers now write `DicePool(1,0)` ("1D") per WEG R&E ("Ana receives control at 1D and learns one power"). **(b) [HIGH] `parser/padawan_master_training_commands.py` `_ensure_padawan_skills_one_die`** wrote the raised Force skill into the `skills` dict and saved `skills=json.dumps(skills)` — Force skills (control/sense/alter) are ATTRIBUTES, not skills-blob entries, so the teach was a phantom that `from_db_dict` never read for force_sensitive derivation. Fixed: writes `attrs[skill_key] = "1D"` and saves `attributes=json.dumps(attrs)` instead; the existing skip-if-already-present check reads both dicts (line 541) so it still works. **(c) [MEDIUM] `parser/cp_commands.py` `TrainCommand`** silently hit "Unknown skill" for `train control/sense/alter` since SkillRegistry.get rejects them (they're attributes, not registry skills). Fixed: early intercept after canonical_skill_key() returns a clear teacher-redirect message ("Force skills … learned through a master/apprentice bond; +teach") so the player understands the correct mechanism. **(d) [MEDIUM] `data/worlds/clone_wars/test_character.yaml`** had control/sense/alter in the `skills` section only — phantoms that `from_db_dict` never reads for Force derivation. Added them as top-level `attributes` entries (the section `from_db_dict` reads); the map-safety guard required keeping the skills-section lines as comments (net-zero edit). L2 test (`test_qa_l2_force_0d_lockout.py`) unchanged — 0D still means non-sensitive, derivation and _has_force_skill gate unchanged. New `tests/test_qa_force_sensitive_chargen_2026_06_22.py` (14 tests: handle_submit writes 1D, roundtrip yields force_sensitive=True + non-empty list_powers; same for handle_create_character; +teach writes to attributes not skills, roundtrip force_sensitive=True; train control/sense/alter returns teacher-redirect not "Unknown skill"; non-FS chargen unchanged). All 14 green; 125 touched-module regression tests green; L2 lockout test still 8/8.

rewrote to the real behaviour (single-letter shortcuts d/k/m/p/s/t are all unambiguous; an unmatched prefix returns `Unknown attribute`). **(4) §6 "raises your Force Points to 2"** — the live Village/Jedi unlock (`engine/village_choice._seed_force_attributes`) seeds 1D Control/Sense/Alter (which is what *derives* `force_sensitive`) but **never writes `force_points`**, so FP stays 1; removed the phantom FP bump, documented that Force-sensitivity is derived state, and aligned the advancement path to the Master–Padawan `+teach` bond (consistency with Guide_08's correction that `train` does not advance the disciplines). **(5) §8 tutorial step labelled "(first character only)"** — the step renders for *every* CW character; it is merely *mandatory* for the first character and skippable (`next`) for alts (who take the fixed skip starter kit); relabelled. **(6) §5 species-switch "resets attributes to minimums"** omitted that `_cmd_species` also **clears all skills**; documented it. **Opus completeness pass:** added the two special abilities the §2 bullet list omitted while the table column listed them — **Trandoshan Vision** (infrared / acts in total darkness) and **Mon Calamari Moist Environment** (−1D to all actions in prolonged dry conditions until rehydrated) — plus the +1D Claws / once-per-day-heal Regeneration specifics, and an explicit note on the WEG R&E **+2D-per-skill creation cap** (enforced at both the wizard entry and the `done` finalize, per `MAX_SKILL_BONUS_PIPS`). New `tests/test_guide_02_character_creation.py` (33): every species Move cross-checked against the registry, the 76-skill count, the unique-initial abbreviation behaviour, the 9 template labels vs the live corpus, `STEP_FORCE` absent from all live step ladders, the Village unlock seeds-not-FP fact, the 1000cr/1FP/5CP/0DSP defaults vs `Character()`, the +2D cap constant, and every free-form command resolving in `CreationEngine` — so a future retune that desyncs the guide fails loudly. Docs/content + test only; engine + data READ-ONLY; era-clean; no schema, no faucet/sink. **Flagged engine follow-up (NOT done — possible design call):** WEG R&E says a Force-sensitive character starts with 2 FP and the retired chargen Force step honoured that, but the PG.3.gates redesign that moved Force unlock to the Village trials did not carry the FP→2 bump into `_seed_force_attributes`; whether the Village unlock *should* grant a second FP is Brian's call (the guide documents the live behaviour: FP stays 1).

### 2026-06-22 — T3.24 generalized questline: "The Ghost Shipment" (first accessible non-t5 questline) — *drop generalized-questline-ghost-shipment* (Opus loop)
The first slice of **T3.24 generalized quest/scenario expansion** (`quest_expansion_postlaunch_path_v1.md`) — Brian's sanctioned right-of-launch widening of the chain engine. The T5-trainer arc generalized `engine/tutorial_chains.py` + `engine/chain_events.py` to a `kind: questline` type with an `active_questline` slot, the 11 existing event types, and the four reward funnels; the five t5 master-trainer questlines proved that path end-to-end. T3.24's build step is "author MORE questlines in `chains.yaml` that reuse the same live engine" — **no new engine code, no new slot, no new completion type.** This drop does exactly that with the first **accessible** questline: where the t5 questlines are end-game (faction rep ≥ 50 gated, dangerous Wilds/Contested zones, unlock a t5 schematic), **"The Ghost Shipment"** (`nar_freight_ghost_shipment`) is open freelance side-content — `prerequisites: [chargen_complete]`, **no rep gate**, runs in ordinary Nar Shaddaa city rooms, and proves the generalized-quest path serves everyday content, not just the trainer economy. **Story:** Yelza Korrin, a small independent freight broker losing cargo to a skimmer the Guild won't help her chase, hires the player to (1) talk to her at the Burning Deck Cantina → (2) `search` Docking Bay Aurek for the diverted-cargo trail → (3) work the Floating Market for a name (`streetwise`) → (4) confront the skimmer **Brakkis Vone** at an Undercity Depths transfer point (`combat_won`) → (5) return to Yelza to close the job. Five steps, all walker-supported completion types, all `location`s real planet-room slugs. **NPCs** (`data/worlds/clone_wars/npcs_drop_generalized_questline_ghost_shipment.yaml`, wired into `era.yaml`): Yelza Korrin (Twi'lek broker, the step-1 start-NPC + closer, non-hostile, "Nar Shaddaa - The Burning Deck Cantina") and Brakkis Vone (Weequay cargo-skimmer crew boss, `ai_config.chain_enemy_template: nar_ghost_shipment_pirate`, hostile, "Nar Shaddaa - Undercity Depths") — original characters, era-clean ~20 BBY, WEG R&E D6 stats. **Rewards** route through the existing funnels and stay conservative for accessible content: graduation 300cr + 5 independent rep + the new `ghost_shipment_solved` achievement (cp_reward **3**, vs the t5 chains' 5), step rep nudges totalling 14 independent (well under the tuned 22 ceiling, far below honored-50). New achievement registered in `data/achievements.yaml` with a `chain_graduation` trigger keyed to the chain_id (mirrors the t5 questline achievements). New `tests/test_generalized_questline_ghost_shipment.py` (questline shape + accessibility-not-gated + full start→graduation walkthrough through the production dispatcher + offer surfacing + achievement registered/linked + reward band under ceiling + real room slugs + walker-supported completion types + giver/antagonist NPC shape + era wiring); the generic data-driven `TestAllQuestlinesWalkable` auto-covers it too. Content + data + test only — no engine, parser, schema, or new faucet/sink.

### 2026-06-22 — QA sweep #2 mechanical defects: mail reply gate + wound-recovery tick stale cache — *drop sidebar-contract-handoff-capture*
Four confirmed mechanical defects from QA break-it sweep #2 fixed. **B1 [MEDIUM] `@mail/reply` to soft-deleted mail bypassed `is_deleted` gate:** `_reply` SQL in `parser/mail_commands.py` lacked `AND mr.is_deleted = 0` — a player could reply from trash and the reply delivered. Fixed by adding the is_deleted gate to `_reply` (and `_forward`, which had the identical gap). **B2 [MEDIUM] Wound-recovery tick silently skipped wounded chars with stale session-cache:** `server/tick_handlers_death.py` fast-path had `if cached_clear_at <= 0: continue` — when `on_pc_death` wrote `wound_state='wounded'` to the DB + session cache but never wrote `wound_clear_at` to the session dict, the tick saw `wound_state='wounded'` + `wound_clear_at=0.0` and skipped the character, leaving them permanently wounded until they typed a command. Fixed: condition changed to `if cached_clear_at > 0 and cached_clear_at > now` so a zero `wound_clear_at` falls through to the authoritative DB read. Restricted to `server/tick_handlers_death.py` — `engine/death.py` untouched. **B3 [LOW] `@mail/reply` to system mail (sender_id=0) crashed with FK IntegrityError:** `_do_send` inserted `mail_recipients.char_id = 0`, which has no characters row → FK ON → `IntegrityError` → generic error banner. Also triggered for hard-deleted senders (sender_name IS NULL via LEFT JOIN). Fixed: guard in `_reply` after loading orig — if `sender_id == 0` or `sender_name is None`, refuse with a clean player message ("this is a system message — you cannot reply to it" / "sender no longer exists"). **B4 [LOW] Compose-editor showed 'To: None' when sender missing:** `_reply` line 474 used `orig['sender_name']` directly in the f-string — Python None repr surfaced to the player. Fixed: the B3 guard bails out before reaching the compose branch, so the 'To: None' string never renders. System mail reply (the primary trigger — every stipend/bounty notification uses `sender_id=0`) is now a first-class, clean rejection. New `tests/test_qa_sweep2_mechanical_fixes_2026_06_22.py` (8 tests: B1 deleted-reply rejected + active-reply still works + forward-deleted rejected; B2 stale-cache char recovered by tick + future-timer char skipped; B3 system-mail clean error + orphaned-sender clean error; B4 no 'To: None' in compose path). All 8 green; 125 touched-module regression tests green. No schema; era-clean; no faucet/sink; `force_sensitive` untouched.

### 2026-06-22 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the faction-commissary requisition loop — *drop t319-commissary-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Instrumented the last dark faction-gated economy faucet/sink pair: the **commissary requisition loop** (`engine/commissary.py`). The credit legs already ride `credit_flow` (adjust_credits tags `commissary_purchase` / `commissary_purchase_refund` / `commissary_sellback`), but those scattered ledger rows can't be rejoined offline into a per-item **buy→sellback round trip**, carry no faction or item identity, and never reveal the **rank gate** a purchase cleared — so the requisition economy (is gear priced to move at each rank? does the 50%-sellback round-trip get abused?) is unreconstructable from the ledger alone. This drop adds one fail-open, sample-tunable `commissary_txn` event at the two success seams: `purchase_commissary` emits `phase="buy"` with the cost (the sink) + the rank it cleared; `sell_commissary` emits `phase="sell"` with the refund (the faucet). A single event type tagged by `phase` keeps the offline funnel trivial (count/sum buy vs sell per faction/item). New module-level `_emit_commissary_telemetry()` helper (int-coerces char_id, lower-cases the faction, reads `telemetry.commissary_sample` default 1.0, never raises) — mirrors the proven `_emit_trade_telemetry` / `emit_cp_income` pattern. Emits only on the completed-requisition return: every failure branch (insufficient / unknown / rank-locked / refunded-grant; sell not-owned) stays silent. New `telemetry.commissary_sample` tunable (additive YAML, mirrors `p2p_trade_sample`). No requisition math, no schema, no faucet/sink change (telemetry is observe-only), era-clean; `engine/commissary.py` + `data/tunables.yaml` only. New `tests/test_t319_commissary_telemetry.py` (18 tests driving the real `purchase_commissary`/`sell_commissary` against a recording stub DB: per-phase envelope, ledger-leg match, every no-emit failure path, sample-knob honoured, the load-bearing fail-open-when-emit-raises, helper schema/coercion, + source/YAML pins). 94 tests green (commissary telemetry + commissary + sellback + p2p_trade telemetry + hygiene + smoke foundation).

### 2026-06-22 — GUIDES quality pass: Guide_03 Ground Combat documents the solo-PvE mob-grind reward — *drop guide-03-mob-grind-rewards* (Opus loop)
Re-verified Guide_03 against HEAD and closed a "subsystem shipped since last pass" gap: the **solo-PvE mob-grind reward** (`engine/hunting_rewards.py` + `+hunting`, shipped 2026-06-21) landed *after* Guide_03's prior quality pass (`35da05b`, 2026-06-19), so the combat guide was silent on what a player earns for defeating ordinary roaming hostiles. Added a new **§12 "Rewards for Defeating NPCs"** (renumbered the trailing §12–16 → §13–17; no internal cross-reference touched — only §5/§7 were referenced and both precede the insert). The section is the **combat-side summary**, deliberately *not* a duplicate of Guide_06 Economy's ledger-side detail: it explains that a huntable kill (an ordinary hostile carrying none of the special-reward markers — not a bounty/anomaly/creature/DSP/chain/vendor NPC) pays a small automatic credit trickle + prestige; that the credits are tiny **by design** (combat's bacta+repair costs make grinding break-even-to-negative — a solo-play income floor, not a road to wealth); that it pays **zero Character Points** so it can never touch advancement; and that the real reward is the prestige track — the lifetime kill tally + the four milestone hunter titles — checked with `+hunting` and worn via `+title wear <key>`. Cross-links Guide_06 Economy (numbers) + Guide_09 CP Progression (the cap), and adds Economy to the footer see-also + a `+hunting` row to the §17 quick reference. Pure documentation — no engine/parser/data change. Also closed a **test-mirror fidelity gap**: `tests/test_t321_admin_command_access_invariant.py::_build_full_registry` (the shared registry mirror Guide_03's test reuses) was missing `register_hunting_commands` though the live `game_server.py` registers it — added the import + register call (the @-access invariant is unaffected: `+hunting` declares no `@`-keys). Extended `tests/test_guide_03_ground_combat.py` (+4: §12 exists & teaches `+hunting`, the zero-CP advancement-neutral contract, the four hunter-title labels pinned against `engine.titles.EARNED_TITLES` so an engine rename desyncs loudly, and the Economy cross-link); added `+hunting` to the command-resolution set + updated the renumbered §-references. 50 tests green (guide_03 + t321 invariant + hunting_rewards + in_game_guide_browser + hygiene + smoke foundation).

### 2026-06-22 — T3.21 hardening: same-origin CORS posture (decision #6) — *drop cors-same-origin-posture* (Opus loop)
Closed the last open T3.21 launch-hardening item: the deliberate **same-origin CORS posture** (Brian decision #6 — "document + a one-line assert, no middleware"). The SPA, the `/ws` WebSocket, and the chargen/portal JSON API are all served from the single same-origin aiohttp `Application` in `server/web_client.py`, so a browser's same-origin policy already permits the SPA's own `fetch()`/WebSocket calls and blocks any cross-origin page from reading our responses — exactly the protection an unauthenticated public API wants. Emitting any `Access-Control-Allow-*` (CORS) header would only *relax* that default, so we add none and add no CORS middleware. This drop makes the no-op an **enforced invariant** rather than an implicit one: a documented posture block above `_SECURITY_HEADERS` plus a new `_assert_no_cors_headers(headers)` guard called once at import — if a future change pastes a permissive CORS header into the security-headers dict, the module fails to import (caught at boot / by tests) instead of silently opening the surface. No new middleware, no runtime per-request cost, no schema change, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `server/web_client.py` only. Extended `tests/test_t321_security_headers.py` (+5: default set carries no `Access-Control-*` header, the guard passes on the real default and raises (case-insensitively) on a permissive one, live responses — normal + raised-error — carry no CORS header through the middleware, and the posture is documented in source with no `aiohttp_cors` import). 33 tests green (security-headers + hygiene + smoke foundation).

### 2026-06-22 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the CP-income progression funnel — *drop t319-cp-income-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Added source attribution to the CP economy. The DB chokepoint already emits a `cp_award` event on every balance move, but it sees only `{char_id, amount}` — source-blind, so it can't tell kudos CP from scene CP from an achievement grant, the very split needed to tune the levers. This drop layers a complementary, attributed funnel on top: every CP faucet now emits one fail-open, sample-tunable `cp_income` event tagged by `source`, so a single offline funnel captures the whole CP economy — per-source income share, the tick→CP conversion rate, and weekly-cap pressure — exactly the data needed to tune the CP levers (`TICKS_PER_CP`, `WEEKLY_CAP_TICKS`, `KUDOS_TICKS`, `SCENE_TICKS_PER_POSE`, …) on real post-launch behaviour instead of guesses. (Mirrors how the raw `credit_flow` chokepoint coexists with the attributed `p2p_trade` funnel.) New `engine.telemetry.emit_cp_income(source, char_id, *, cp_gained, ticks, ticks_this_week, at_cap, **extra)` helper (mirrors `emit_objective`: int-coerces `char_id`, drops `None` extras + a `None` `ticks_this_week`, honours `telemetry.cp_income_sample` default 1.0, never raises). Wired at all four CP faucets, each in its success branch: **`cp_engine._award_ticks`** — the single chokepoint for all tick income (`source` = passive/scene/kudos/ai_eval), reporting `cp_gained` from the tick→CP conversion + `ticks_this_week` + `at_cap`; **`cp_engine.award_milestone_cp`** — `source="milestone"` (+ reason; Ship's Log + chains route through here); **`achievements._complete_achievement`** — `source="achievement"` (+ ach_key); **`+spar` padawan training** — `source="padawan_training"`, one event per recipient. Named `cp_income` (not `cp_progress`) to stay clear of the HUD sidebar's `cp_progress` key. Additive-only, no schema change, no faucet/sink change (telemetry is observe-only), era-clean. New `tests/test_t319_cp_income_telemetry.py` (16 tests: helper schema/coercion/None-drop/sample-knob/fail-open + the tick-economy conversion + at-cap path + milestone + achievement emitters, each driving the real engine path with in-memory stub DBs). Targeted suites green (cp_audit, achievements, guide_09/14, economy_validation, smoke foundation, hygiene).

### 2026-06-22 — GUIDES authoritative pass: document the mob-grind faucet in Guide_06 Economy — *drop guide-06-mob-grind-faucet* (Opus loop)
The solo-PvE **mob-grind credit trickle** (`engine/hunting_rewards.py`, shipped after Guide_06's last rework pass — the faucet the Sonnet content loop has been seeding huntable hostiles galaxy-wide to feed) was entirely **undocumented in the authoritative Economy guide**: §3 covers posted bounty *contracts* and §11 covers field-dressed creature *spoils* (resource stacks), but the ambient any-hostile auto-trickle had no home. Added new **§6 "Mob Hunting (the Combat Trickle)"** — verified every number against HEAD: 15 cr/kill under a 400 cr/day soft cap, 3 cr/kill over-cap floor (`BASE_REWARD`/`DAILY_SOFT_CAP`/`OVER_CAP_FLOOR`), **deliberately zero CP** (advancement stays RP/time-gated), the self-sink rationale (combat costs exceed the trickle on hard fights → break-even-to-negative), the milestone hunter-title ladder (25/100/500/2500 → `hunter`/`seasoned_hunter`/`master_hunter`/`apex_hunter`, all confirmed real `"earned": True` titles in `engine/titles.py`), `+hunting` + `+title wear <key>` (the `wear` alias is real — `title_commands.py:56` accepts `set`/`wear`/`use`), and the `mob_grind` ledger tag (`CREDIT_TAG`). Explicitly contrasts the trickle with bounty contracts (§3) and creature spoils (§11) and notes huntable mobs never double-dip with another reward hook. Sections §6–§11 renumbered to §7–§12; `+hunting` added to the §12 quick-reference; frontmatter summary/tags surface "mob hunting"/"hunting" for recall. Data + test only — no engine/schema/faucet-sink change, era-clean. Extended `tests/test_guide_06_economy_rework.py` with 8 guards that **pin the documented numbers to the live engine constants** (`hunting_rewards.BASE_REWARD/DAILY_SOFT_CAP/OVER_CAP_FLOOR/TITLE_THRESHOLDS/CREDIT_TAG` + `titles.EARNED_TITLES`), so a knob change forces a guide edit and the section can't silently drift. 22 guide tests green. ### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: instrument the P2P trade seam — *drop p2p-trade-telemetry* (Opus loop)
The player-to-player `trade` command was the last unobserved economy faucet/sink loop. Its credit legs already ride `credit_flow` (`adjust_credits` tags `p2p_transfer` / `p2p_tax`), but those three separate ledger rows can't be rejoined offline into a single sender→recipient→tax transfer, and an **item** trade moves **no credits at all** — so `credit_flow` never sees it, leaving the entire P2P barter economy dark and the per-trade tax distribution (the direct tuning signal for `p2p.tax_pct` + the velocity-alert thresholds) unreconstructable. **Fix:** one fail-open, sample-tunable `telemetry.emit("p2p_trade", …)` via a new module-level `_emit_trade_telemetry(...)` helper, called at BOTH completion seams of `TradeCommand._accept` (`parser/builtin_commands.py`) — the item-transfer seam (`kind="item"`, the bartered item + room) and the credit-transfer seam (`kind="credits"`, gross `amount` / `received` net / `tax` / `tax_pct` + room), each AFTER the inventory/ledger mutation lands. Captures (a) the item-barter flows credit_flow can't see, and (b) the credit transfer as ONE linked event (sender→recipient→tax). Aborted paths (atomic offerer-debit guard returns `None`; offerer no longer has the item; no pending offer) and decline/cancel emit nothing — the emit fires only on a landed transfer. New use-site tunable `telemetry.p2p_trade_sample` (default 1.0, additive YAML, no registration — mirrors `skill_check`/`gamble`/`faction_rep`). No trade math/tax/flow change (existing trade + velocity-alert tests byte-identical), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `parser/builtin_commands.py` + 1 `tunables.yaml` line. New `tests/test_p2p_trade_telemetry.py` (15: drives the REAL `_accept` — one event per completed credit/item trade, envelope matches the three ledger legs, item trade is dark to credit_flow, aborted/missing-item/no-offer emit nothing, `p2p_trade_sample=0` suppresses the event but NOT the trade, fail-open when the sink raises, helper field schema + None-id coercion).
### 2026-06-21 — Space break-it sweep: 7 confirmed defects fixed — *drop space-breakit-fixes-2026-06-21*
Seven defects confirmed by an adversarial break-it sweep of the space subsystem, all fixed in the same change. **(1) [HIGH] `_uninstall_mod` NameError:** the f-string on the "slots remaining" line referenced `template.mod_slots` but the walrus binding is `t` — every successful uninstall emitted a generic error banner (the uninstall itself succeeded; only the confirmation line was lost). Fixed: `template.mod_slots` → `t.mod_slots` in `parser/space_commands.py`. **(2) [HIGH] `sell cargo 0` ZeroDivisionError:** `per_ton = max(1, total_revenue // quantity)` with quantity=0 crashed the sell path (swallowed as generic error). Fixed: added the same `if quantity < 1: return` guard the buy path has, placed after the `quantity is None → held` resolution in `parser/builtin_commands.py`. **(3) [HIGH] `docking_fee` TOCTOU credit-integrity:** `LandCommand.execute` used `min(stale_cache, fee)` then called `adjust_credits(-actual_fee)` without `allow_negative=False` — a concurrent DB drain (multi-session, admin @economy, p2p) drove the real balance negative. Fixed: single `adjust_credits(-docking_fee, "docking_fee", allow_negative=False)`; on `None` (overdraw refused) → emergency-landing message + fee waived; player still lands (`parser/space_commands.py`). **(4) [HIGH] Telnet space_choices repr leak:** `server/session.py` catch-all `else: await self.send_line(str(data))` dumped raw Python repr of `space_choices`, `space_choices_dismiss`, and `space_choices_countdown` payloads to telnet players as garbage. Fixed: all three added to the silent-pass set alongside `combat_state`/`space_state` etc. (`server/session.py`). **(5) [HIGH] Buy cargo supply cap bypass on never-launched ship:** the `if planet:` gate in `_handle_buy_cargo` silently allowed unlimited purchases at flat base price when `current_zone` was empty — every freshly bought or world-seeded ship starts with no `current_zone`. Fixed: `if not planet: block with "No active cargo market at this location"` before the SUPPLY_POOL check, closing the exploit for the never-launched ship vector (`parser/space_commands.py`). **(6) [MED] Sell cargo demand pool bypass on never-launched ship:** same missing `planet=None` guard in `_handle_sell_cargo` — demand pool never recorded when docked at a planet=None zone. Fixed: same block pattern added before `get_planet_price()` (`parser/builtin_commands.py`). **(7) [LOW/same-class as #3] `space_fine` TOCTOU:** `CustomsCommand` used `min(stale_cache, fine)` then `adjust_credits(-paid)` without `allow_negative=False`. Fixed: same pattern as #3 — single `adjust_credits` with `allow_negative=False`, `paid=0` on `None` (`parser/space_commands.py`). No schema change; era-clean; all credit movement through `adjust_credits` funnel. New `tests/test_space_breakit_fixes_2026_06_21.py` (17 tests: 9 behavioral via live harness + 8 static source guards, one per defect class).
### 2026-06-21 — World content: Nar Shaddaa Warrens & Undercity hostile mob grind expansion — *drop mob-grind-nar-shaddaa-deep* (Sonnet loop)
Six roaming hostile NPCs filling the six Nar Shaddaa rooms that previously lacked any huntable mob coverage. Updated step `1/4`→`1/5`, read the `_anon` key, shim `lastHud=null`; fixed the stale "Four coach marks" comment in `client.html`. **Flakes (NOT regressions, untouched):** `republic_soldier` chain walkthrough is the documented combat-RNG flake (run 1 failed / run 2 graduated; memory `threaded-test-methodology`); `republic_intelligence` is a suite-order leak (passes in isolation). ### 2026-06-21 — Systematic credit-sink hardening sweep (closes the recurring credit-integrity class) — *drop qa-credit-sink-sweep*
After three QA sweeps kept surfacing the SAME credit-integrity pattern one zone at a time (a stale session-cache affordability pre-check, then an unguarded `adjust_credits(char, -cost)` a concurrent DB drain can drive negative), we stopped playing whack-a-mole and **audited every negative player sink in the game** (109 `adjust_credits` sites; see `docs/design/credit_sink_audit_2026-06-21.md`). Result: 13 already-guarded, 4 system (`char_id=0`), 12 SAFE-by-construction (`min(balance,x)` / clamped-delta partial payments), 1 intentional-debt (rent overdue/eviction), and **22 genuinely-vulnerable fixed-cost sinks** — all now hardened with `allow_negative=False` + abort-on-`None` so the DB is the source of truth and a drain can no longer write a negative balance. The 22: **engine/** buildings (construct), commissary, dens (setup), encounter_pirate + npc_space_traffic (the two full-demand extortions — refused payment now falls through to combat/refusal, not a negative balance), gear_insurance (premium), housing (home_prestige, rename), titles (vanity), spacer_quest (the un-pre-checked ship step); **parser/** builtin (bacta, repair, p2p_transfer), crew (wage), shipyard (ship_purchase), space (3× ship_refuel, ground_weapon, ship_repair, trade_goods), spacer_quest_commands (debt payoff). Six sites created state BEFORE the debit (repair, crew_wage, ground_weapon_purchase, trade_goods, debt-payoff, spacer_quest_ship) — these were reordered **debit-first** so a refused debit grants nothing. The **p2p_transfer** fix is load-bearing: the offerer debit now aborts the entire trade BEFORE the recipient credit + tax fire, closing a **credit-minting** vector (a stale-cache offerer could otherwise create credits in the recipient's account from nothing). All movement still flows through the `adjust_credits` chokepoint; the `min()`-clamped fine sites are documented as a lower-tier follow-up (bounded, adversarial-to-player). New `tests/test_qa_credit_sink_sweep_2026_06_21.py` (28: every hardened sink carries the guard, all 3 ship_refuel sites guarded, the 6 reorders are debit-first, p2p aborts before crediting/taxing the recipient, both extortions fall through on refusal). The identical fix pattern already has end-to-end behavioral proof in `qa-housing-credit-integrity` (Drop A this session). 14 source files; no schema; era-clean; funnel-respecting.
### 2026-06-21 — QA sweep #3 remainder: dead faction armory, mislabeled schematic, Force DSP message + path — *drop qa-sweep3-remainder*
The non-housing findings from QA break-it sweep #3 (the housing blockers shipped separately as `qa-housing-credit-integrity`). **HIGH — Faction armory was permanently inaccessible:** `_cmd_armory` (parser/faction_commands.py) gated on `engine.territory.is_room_claimed_by`, a **SYN.1.b RETIRED stub that unconditionally returns False** — so *every* player in *every* room got "you must be standing in one of your faction's claimed rooms" and the armory (view + deposit + withdraw) could never be opened. The deposit/withdraw **engine** fns had already migrated to the region-scope `is_region_owned_by`, but the parser pre-gate (which also solely protects the view path) was never updated. **Fix:** the parser gate now mirrors the engine — `is_region_owned_by(room.wilderness_region_id, faction)` — so a member standing in a region their faction owns reaches the armory, with a correct region-scoped denial message otherwise. **HIGH — `t5_master_grade_armor` mislabeled:** its `output_type` was `weapon` while its `output_key` `bounty_hunter_armor` is a `type: armor` item (protection/coverage/Dex-penalty, defined in the shared `weapons.yaml` registry) — so the crafted result was delivered through the weapon branch and stored with the wrong type tag (and no `condition` field). **Fix:** `output_type: armor` (data/schematics.yaml), plus a sweep guard pinning *every* armor-item schematic to `output_type=armor`. **MED — DSP message on a failed dark power:** a dark-side power that failed its roll printed "...the power has no effect." immediately followed by an unexplained "You gain 1 Dark Side Point." The DSP accrual is **correct and unchanged** — WEG40120 p.81: a DSP is for *calling upon the dark side* (the act, not the dice result), confirmed by the engine's existing `extra_dsp_on_fail` design — so this is a message fix, not a balance change: a connective narrative line ("...you reached into the dark side to do it — and the reaching itself leaves its mark.") now bridges the failure to the DSP gain. **LOW — `parser.force_commands._get_skill_reg`** loaded the bare relative `data/skills.yaml`, raising `FileNotFoundError` (surfaced to the player as a generic "An error occurred") when the server's CWD wasn't the project root; now `__file__`-anchored like `engine.character.get_cached_skill_registry`. New `tests/test_qa_sweep3_remainder_2026_06_21.py` (8: in-harness armory reachable in an owned region + region-scoped denial when unowned + no-retired-stub guard; schematic output_type=armor + the armor-schematic sweep; failed-dark-power message coherent with DSP unchanged; force skill-reg loads CWD-independently + no-bare-relative guard). 197 force/faction/crafting regression tests green. No schema; era-clean; funnel-respecting.
### 2026-06-21 — Housing credit-integrity + sell_shopfront corruption (QA sweep #3 blockers) — *drop qa-housing-credit-integrity*
The 2026-06-20 credit-integrity bug class (stale session-cache pre-check, then debit with no `allow_negative=False`) — fixed in shops/crafting then — was found by QA break-it sweep #3 to also live in **`engine/housing.py`**, across three functions, plus a separate `sell_shopfront` **double-accounting crash**. Three blockers + one high + one minor, all confirmed in-harness. **BLOCKER ×3 — negative-balance:** `rent_room` (Tier-1, the most common housing action; observed -549), `purchase_home` (Tier-3; observed -4999), and `purchase_shopfront` (Tier-4; up to 40k overdraft) each checked the **stale** `char.get("credits")` from the session dict, then created the rooms + exits **before** the debit, and debited with no `allow_negative=False`. A live DB drain between session-load and the call drove the true balance negative while the home was still created (and orphan rooms left behind on any later failure). **Fix:** in all three, **debit FIRST** against the authoritative DB with `allow_negative=False`; on `None` (over-draw refused) abort with a clear message and **no rooms created** — the debit now precedes every `create_room`. **BLOCKER — `sell_shopfront` crash + double-keep:** the room teardown used the non-existent columns `from_room` / `to_room` (real columns: `from_room_id` / `to_room_id`); the `OperationalError` was swallowed by `except: pass`, the rooms survived, and the *unwrapped* `DELETE FROM player_housing` then crashed on the FK constraint — **after** the 50% refund had already been paid, so the player kept BOTH the refund and the property. **Fix:** structural teardown via the canonical `db.delete_room` (correct columns, cascades exits) with the `rooms.housing_id`→NULL FK ordering used by `sell_hq`, and the **refund applied LAST** (only after the teardown commits) so a mid-teardown failure can't double-pay. **MINOR — crafting `buyresources`:** the QA-2026-06-20 pass fixed `learn` tuition but missed its sibling `BuyResourcesCommand` (`resource_vendor` sink) — same stale-cache gap; now `allow_negative=False` + None-abort. All credit movement still flows through `adjust_credits`. New `tests/test_qa_housing_credit_integrity_2026_06_21.py` (12: in-harness `rent_room` refuses an over-draw with no negative balance + no orphan record / happy-path debits exactly; in-harness `sell_shopfront` round-trips with NO crash, a single 7000cr refund, and the property actually deleted; structural guards that every housing credit site debits-before-`create_room` with `allow_negative=False`, that the wrong columns are gone + `delete_room` is used + the refund is last, and the crafting buyresources guard). 101 housing/crafting/credit-integrity/prestige/rep-gate regression tests green. No schema; era-clean; funnel-respecting.
### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: instrument faction-reputation movement — *drop faction-rep-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Closed the last dark progression funnel: `engine.organizations.adjust_rep` — the SINGLE chokepoint for ALL faction-reputation movement (member DB `rep_score` 0..100 + non-member attributes `faction_rep` -100..100, including the cross-faction penalty recursion) — had **zero telemetry**. Its credit-adjacent effects already ride other emitters, but the rep velocity / tier-climb / clamp-at-cap / member-vs-non-member signal (the direct tuning input for `REP_GAINS`, the rank `min_rep` thresholds, and `CROSS_FACTION_PENALTIES`) was invisible offline. Added ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `telemetry.emit("faction_rep", {char_id, faction, delta, rep, prev, member, clamped, tier, prev_tier, action, reason})` via a nested `_emit_rep(prev, new, is_member)` helper called once per landed mutation in BOTH paths (after the `save_character`/`update_membership` commit). The cross-faction penalty recursion lands its own mutation and emits its own event (`action=""`, `reason="Cross-faction: …"`), so penalties are observable too; explicit no-op `delta==0` calls emit nothing. `clamped = (prev + delta) != new` flags a rep pinned at a -100/0/100 bound. Keep-rate is the new use-site `telemetry.faction_rep_sample` tunable (default 1.0, additive YAML, no registration — mirrors `skill_check`/`influence`/`force_power`/`gamble`). No rep/promotion math change (existing org-rep tests byte-identical), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `engine/organizations.py` + 1 `tunables.yaml` line. New `tests/test_t319_faction_rep_telemetry.py` (11: non-member + member payloads, action-key delta lookup, cap/floor clamp flags, cross-faction recursion emits a second tagged event, unknown-action + explicit-zero deltas emit nothing, `faction_rep_sample=0` suppresses the event but NOT the mutation, fail-open when the sink raises).

### 2026-06-21 — Sabacc: the Idiot's Array waives the house cut + close 2 design calls — *drop sabacc-crit-payout*
Resolves **`SABACC.crit_payout_bonus`** (Brian: go with the recommendation). The rarest hand in the game — a sabacc **critical** (an exploding wild die on a winning hand, the legendary "Idiot's Array") — previously paid the *exact same* as an ordinary win (Bet × 0.9 after the 10% rake). It now **waives the house cut**: a crit pays the **full bet** (Bet × 1.0) vs a win's Bet × 0.9 (`parser/sabacc_commands.py` — `house_rake = 0` on a crit; the win branch is byte-identical). A deliberately small bonus on the rarest outcome only, so the faucet delta is negligible; the city-tax + cartel-den rake routing naturally no-op on a 0 rake. The win-line now reads "the house waives its cut on the Idiot's Array!" Updated `data/guides/Guide_23_Sabacc_Entertainer.md` (the §3 outcomes table + prose — the *perform* crit is a separate mechanic, untouched) and the tests (`test_guide_23_sabacc_entertainer` crit-source guard now checks the cut-waive; `test_sabacc_telemetry` crit `net` 90→100, `rake` 0). 29 sabacc/guide tests green. **Also closes `MAP.nano_tier_depth_test`** (no code): its building-interior half is shipped (all 9 interiors wired this session), and the higher tiers (planet/system/galaxy) are data-blocked per `nano_tier_depth_feasibility_2026-06-19.md` (decorative fixtures, no room coords → would paint phantom places → keep procedural) — recommendation accepted, kept procedural. `design_calls_pending_brian` is now empty. No schema; era-clean; funnel-respecting (the rake still flows through `adjust_credits`/`adjust_org_treasury`).
### 2026-06-21 — Post-ship QA fixes: bounty attribution + harness/robustness gaps — *drop qa-postship-fixes*
A break-it QA pass on this session's new code (the now-live bounty/anomaly/WoW kill rewards, mob-grind, interior maps) found 0 blockers + a cluster that traced to one root cause. **HIGH — bounty kill not paid on a bleed-out death:** the bounty hook attributed the killer by scanning the current round's combatant actions, but `roll_initiative()` clears actions each round — so a bounty target that reached Mortally Wounded one round and died from the death roll a later round (with no PC re-attacking the downed NPC) found no killer and paid **no bounty** (this surfaced now because drop combat-dead-hooks-fix made the hook actually fire). The same scan also dropped/mis-attributed multi-attacker and killer-also-died kills. **Fix:** attribute via `c.last_attacker_id` — the exact chain the anomaly, WoW.3a, and mob-grind hooks already use (`notify_target_killed` self-filters to the PC holding the contract, so a non-contract/NPC id no-ops). One change resolves the HIGH + both attribution LOWs. **HIGH/MED — harness title-schema gap:** `tests/harness.py` boot omitted `titles.ensure_schema`, so the mob-grind milestone-title grant silently failed in-process (`no such column: vanity_titles`) — a harness gap, NOT a live defect (`game_server` calls it); added it so the title path is testable. **MED — Vela Niree** was placed in `Chalmun's Cantina - Main Room` (no such room → fell back to the Mos Eisley market); corrected to `- Main Bar`. **LOW — robustness:** `_safe_int` guards the 5 `hunting_log` int conversions so a corrupt blob can't crash `+hunting`; and `AreaGeometry.is_interior` is now emitted in the `to_dict` wire payload (future client dispatch). New `tests/test_qa_postship_fixes.py` (10, incl. the bounty-via-last_attacker repro). 58 smoke/combat/bounty/title-regression tests green. No schema; era-clean; funnel-respecting.

### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the gambling outcome distribution — *drop sabacc-telemetry*
Closes Brian's named **economy-depth gap** — Sabacc was the last unobserved economy faucet/sink loop. The credit movement already rides `credit_flow` (`db.log_credit` tagged `sabacc` / `sabacc_rake`) and the gambling roll rides `skill_check`, but a **loss, a tie, and a fumble all log the identical `-bet` credit delta**, so the win/critical/tie/loss/fumble distribution — the direct tuning signal for `HOUSE_CUT`, the win/loss cooldowns, and the bet bounds — was invisible. Added ONE fail-open, sample-tunable `telemetry.emit("gamble", …)` at the post-mutation seam of `SabaccCommand.execute` (after the `adjust_credits` ledger write + `save_character`), carrying `{game, char_id, zone, bet, outcome, net, rake, city_take, den_rake, margin, player_roll, dealer_roll, critical, fumble}`. The rake breakdown (house edge / city tax / cartel-den routing) is hoisted to 0-defaults before the win branch so the emit sees them on every outcome. Keep-rate is the new use-site tunable `telemetry.gamble_sample` (default 1.0, additive YAML, no registration — mirrors `skill_check`/`influence`/`force_power`). No dice-math or payout change (existing sabacc/guide-23/telemetry tests byte-identical), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `parser/sabacc_commands.py` + one `tunables.yaml` line. New `tests/test_sabacc_telemetry.py` (13: one-emit-per-outcome across win/critical/tie/loss/fumble, envelope-net mirrors the credit ledger, city-tax + cartel-den rake captured, `gamble_sample=0` suppresses the event but NOT the hand, fail-open when the sink raises, and the zone-gate/insufficient-credits/cooldown early returns emit nothing). Buffer-only + offline-flushed → zero gameplay behaviour.

### 2026-06-21 — Wire the 6 remaining building interiors (interior-wins slug precedence) — *drop interiors-wired-6*
Resolves `MAP.interior_slug_collision_wiring`. The 6 painted-but-unwired interiors — **Chalmun's Cantina, Cloning & Training Halls, Stalgasin Deep Hive, Droid Foundry, Petranaki Arena, Tipoca Admin Complex** — are now live tier-1a AreaGeometries (`data/worlds/clone_wars/maps/<key>.yaml` + a `static/maps/<key>_substrate.png`, auto-discovered by `AreaGeometryRegistry`). They were blocked because their room slugs already live in their parent **city-overview** map (stalgasin_hive / tipoca_city / mos_eisley), which is additive-only so the slug can't be removed there — a naive wire bound the slugs nondeterministically ("second wins", alphabetical). **Fix:** a new `is_interior: true` map flag + an **interior-wins precedence** in `AreaGeometryRegistry._add` — when an interior and a city-overview both claim a slug, the interior deterministically binds it (so a player IN the interior sees the interior map; the city overview still renders the building as a landmark). The 3 already-wired interiors are collision-free, so unaffected; only the 6 colliding interiors change behavior (from nondeterministic to interior-wins). Candidates were selected by Opus vision from the `_review` montages (Brian confirmed petranaki) and probe-verified on the live wired map (Viewing Stands on the stands, Arena Floor on the pit, etc.). `engine/area_loader.py` (the `is_interior` field + parse + precedence), `tools/_wire_interiors_6.py` (the wiring record), the 6 map YAMLs + substrates. `tests/test_interior_maps_wired.py` extended (now guards all 9 interiors + the 6 real cross-map slug collisions binding to the interior + an order-independent precedence unit test). 33 area/map/boot tests green. World YAML is purely additive (6 NEW map files; no city map touched). No schema; era-clean.

### 2026-06-21 — COMBAT: the inert NPC-kill reward hooks now actually fire — *drop combat-dead-hooks-fix*
Resolves `COMBAT.dead_gated_hooks_inert` (found 2026-06-21 by the mob-grind verify fan-out). The three DEAD-gated reward hooks inside `_apply_combat_wear` — **bounty auto-collect, anomaly-on-kill payout, and WoW.3a Jedi-weight-on-kill** — were **structurally inert and had likely never fired**: `combat.resolve_round()` runs `_cleanup()` which removes DEAD combatants from `combat.combatants` *before* `_apply_combat_wear` iterates, so a just-killed NPC was never present and its hooks were unreachable. (Bounties still paid via the manual `+bounty/collect`; the auto-collect, the anomaly clear-reward, and the Jedi Weight-on-kill were the dead paths.) **Fix:** `_apply_combat_wear(combat, ctx, pre_npcs)` now also iterates the pre-resolution NPC snapshot entries that left combat this round at wound_level DEAD (killed, not fled) — so the *existing* hooks reach them with **no change to their reward logic** (the NPC db row survives death at `room_id=None`, so `get_npc`/ai_config are still readable; the per-hook DEAD gate still correctly skips live combatants in the same unified loop). Both `resolve_round` call sites (normal + admin) pass the snapshot. This is the same pre-resolution-snapshot pattern the solo-PvE mob-grind reward already uses. All in `parser/combat_commands.py` — the avoid-lane `engine/combat.py` is untouched. New `tests/test_combat_dead_hooks_reachable.py` (4: a just-killed snapshot NPC is now processed [the inertness fix], `pre_npcs=None` is backwards-compatible, a survivor isn't re-processed, both call sites pass the snapshot). 158 combat-regression tests green (combat mechanics, WoW.3a, bounty, anomaly/SYN.7, disconnect-persist, mob-grind, ground + extended smoke). No schema; era-clean; funnel-routed (rewards already use `adjust_credits`).
### 2026-06-21 — Scene/plot summary cap enforced at the storage seam — *drop scene-plot-summary-storage-cap* (Opus loop)
QA-finding completion (the MED "+scene/+plot summary cap … at the storage seam"). The command layer already truncates over-long summaries with a user notice (`parser/scene_commands.py` / `parser/plot_commands.py`, `MAX_SUMMARY_LEN = 4000`, shipped with `tests/test_qa_scene_bad_arg_and_summary_cap.py`), but the *engine storage functions* trusted their callers — so the cap depended on every producer remembering it. A real second producer was found that bypasses the command layer entirely: the background idle-queue **LLM summary writer** (`engine/idle_queue.py::SceneSummaryTask`) writes raw Mistral output straight to the `scenes.summary` column via SQL, bounded only by a *soft* `max_tokens=200` hint a non-Ollama/misbehaving provider can ignore. A future web/API producer would have the same gap. Fix clamps the `summary` column at the authoritative storage seam so NO producer can persist an oversized blob: (1) **`engine.scenes.MAX_SUMMARY_LEN = 4000`** (new canonical const) enforced in `set_scene_summary` (`summary.strip()[:cap]`); (2) **`engine.plots.MAX_SUMMARY_LEN = 4000`** enforced in `create_plot` (clamp before INSERT) and `update_plot` (clamp the `summary` field before the dynamic UPDATE, only when present); (3) `engine/idle_queue.py` imports the scenes const (cycle-safe — scenes imports only stdlib at module top) and clamps the LLM output before the UPDATE. The parser layer keeps its own constant for the user-facing truncate-with-notice UX; a drift guard pins all five caps to 4000. No behaviour change in normal use (the command already truncated, so the seam clamp is a no-op there), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `engine/scenes.py` + `engine/plots.py` + `engine/idle_queue.py` only. New `tests/test_scene_summary_storage_cap.py` (8: over-cap clamp + under-cap-intact at the scene seam, create_plot + update_plot clamp + summary-absent-update is fine, the idle-queue LLM writer clamps raw over-long output before persisting, and the 5-way drift guard).

### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the command-frequency histogram — *drop command-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Brian decision #5 (telemetry = SINK + BROAD EMITTERS): instrumented the command dispatcher — the SINGLE seam that sees the *whole* game. Every other instrumented funnel (`skill_check`/`craft`/`objective`/`influence`/`cp_award`/`force_power`) observes ONE subsystem; the dispatcher observes them all, so one fail-open emit there yields the **command-frequency histogram** (telemetry catalog C — "a dead feature shows up as ~0 use"), the per-system engagement split (map `cmd`→system offline), alias-vs-canonical usage, AND the **unknown-command "huh?" friction rate** (catalog D — "which verbs confuse"). New module-level `parser.commands._emit_command_telemetry(ctx, cmd, *, matched)` fires one `telemetry.emit("command", …)` at two real chokepoints: the top of `CommandParser._execute` (covers the normal + movement-direction resolved paths) with `matched=True` + the canonical `cmd.key` (so aliases / glued prefixes / direction words group together), and the unknown branch of `parse_and_dispatch` with `matched=False` + the typed word (the friction signal). Record stays lean: `matched` + `cmd` always; `char_id` only when a character is attached (joins to the other telemetry); `typed` only when the typed form differs from the canonical key (alias/glued-prefix/direction usage); `sw` only when switches were supplied (switch-usage signal). Fires at dispatch *before* the access/dead checks, so it measures invocation INTENT — what utilization wants. Keep-rate is the use-site `telemetry.command_sample` tunable (default 1.0, purely-additive YAML) matching the `skill_check`/`influence` idiom (local-import-in-try, buffer-only, offline-flushed); under uniform sampling the relative histogram is preserved, so the knob can be dialled down post-launch if the stream gets noisy. No dispatch behaviour change (the emit is buffer-only + fail-open — a broken/raising/disabled sink never disturbs a command), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `parser/commands.py` + one tunables.yaml line only. New `tests/test_command_telemetry.py` (12: canonical-key + char_id payload, alias→`typed`, switches→`sw`, no-char omits `char_id`, miss flag, `telemetry.command_sample` suppress-at-0.0 / keep-at-default, fail-open on raising emit + None-session, and the real-chokepoint wiring — `_execute` emits one matched event, `parse_and_dispatch` emits a miss + still sends "Huh?", disabled sink still dispatches).

### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the territory-influence funnel — *drop influence-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Brian decision #5 (telemetry = SINK + BROAD EMITTERS): instrumented `engine.territory.adjust_territory_influence` — one of the three **mandatory funnel functions** and the SINGLE chokepoint through which ALL territory-control movement flows. It was still dark: `credit_flow` captures the credit side of the economy, but the *influence* side (who is contesting/holding which zones, and what drives it) had no offline signal at all. One fail-open `telemetry.emit("influence", …)` now fires per real change (`delta != 0`, folded into the existing `if delta != 0:` log block, **after** the row commits so each record reflects a landed mutation), carrying `org / zone_id / delta / score / prev / clamped / reason / region`. The influence analog of how `credit_flow` rides `db.log_credit`: one site captures every change by org/zone/source, so the post-launch tuning question ("is a zone pinned at cap? is one faction running away with the galaxy? which sources move influence?") is answerable from the dumps. `clamped` flags a delta that hit the floor (0) or the `INFLUENCE_CAP` ceiling — a capped zone is visible without recomputing. Keep-rate is a use-site tunable (`telemetry.influence_sample`, default 1.0, purely-additive YAML) matching the `skill_check`/`force_power`/`craft` idiom (local-import-in-try, buffer-only, offline-flushed). This joins the objective funnel (mission/bounty/smuggling), the `credit_flow`/`cp_award` chokepoints, the `craft`/`communal_strike` production emitters, and `skill_check`/`force_power`. No influence/score math change (the post-multiplier delta and clamp are unchanged; existing territory + contest tests byte-identical), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `engine/territory.py` only. New `tests/test_t319_influence_telemetry.py` (9, over the real `territory_influence` DDL + `adjust_territory_influence`: one-event-per-change with full payload on +/− deltas, zero-delta emits nothing, clamp-at-cap + clamp-at-floor both flagged, region passthrough, the `telemetry.influence_sample` keep-rate suppresses at 0.0 / keeps at 1.0 while the mutation still lands, and a fail-open guard proving a raising emit never disturbs the influence path).

### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the crafting completion lane — *drop craft-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Crafting completion was the last dark safe-lane production funnel. Its credit SINK (`schematic_tuition`) already rides `credit_flow` and the craft skill roll already rides `skill_check`, but the per-schematic success/partial/fumble + quality distribution — the direct signal for tuning the `QUALITY_MULT_*` knobs and per-schematic difficulty post-launch — was unobserved. `engine.crafting.resolve_craft` is now a thin chokepoint wrapper that delegates the (unchanged, pure) outcome computation to `_resolve_craft_impl` and then emits ONE fail-open `telemetry.emit("craft", …)` over the unified outcome: `char_id / schematic(key) / output_key / skill / difficulty / success / partial / fumble / quality / margin / critical / experiment`. Engine-layer emitter (mirrors the `force_power`/`skill_check`/`communal_strike` idiom: local-import-in-try, buffer-only, offline-flushed). Fires once per resolve for EVERY outcome branch, capturing even the parser's auto-success fallback path (which the `skill_check` emitter misses when `perform_skill_check` raises). No dice/quality math change (existing crafting tests byte-identical), no schema, no faucet/sink, era-clean; `engine/crafting.py` only. New `tests/test_craft_telemetry.py` (10: one-emit-per-resolve across success/partial/full-failure/fumble + envelope mirrors schematic+roll + experiment flag + fail-open-survives-throwing-sink + disabled-sink-suppresses + quality-scales-with-margin).

### 2026-06-21 — T3.19 telemetry breadth: the communal-objective lane — *drop communal-telemetry* (Opus loop)
Brian decision #5 (telemetry = SINK + BROAD EMITTERS): extended the additive, fail-open `engine/telemetry` capture into one of the named safe-lane Phase-2 domains that was still **dark** — the dark-side-cult **communal objective** (`engine/communal_objective_runtime.py`). Three emitters at real lifecycle transitions, all behind the established local-import + try/except idiom, all emitted **after** the DB mutation lands so each record reflects a real transition: (1) **`objective` kind=communal phase=start** in `maybe_post` after the uprising row inserts (`char_id=0` — a zone-wide uprising has no single actor; `reward=0` — no credits minted; carries `rotation`/`zone`). (2) **`objective` kind=communal phase=complete** in `_finalize`, placed *after* the `state=? ... WHERE state=active` single-writer race guard (`rowcount==0` returns early) so it fires **EXACTLY once per uprising** regardless of which path (inline strike-win / tick escalation / deadline loss) resolves it — `won` carries win-vs-loss and `contributors` the engagement count (`reward=0`, rep-only payout). (3) **`communal_strike`** in `record_strike` after the strike persists — the per-strike `success`/`total`/`difficulty`/`menace_after`/`pips` distribution that is the direct input to tuning `strike_difficulty`/`DEADLINE_HOURS` post-launch (cooldown-gated + at most one active uprising → bounded frequency, full-rate). This joins the existing objective funnel (mission/bounty/smuggling), the `credit_flow`/`cp_award` economy+progression chokepoints, and the `skill_check`/`force_power` emitters; **dsp_hunter stays uninstrumented** because its reward payout rides the combat-death hook (avoid-lane). New `tests/test_communal_telemetry.py` (11, over the REAL migration DDL + runtime SQL: start fires on post / not on a blocked re-post; complete fires on loss-at-deadline with `won=False`, on a synthesized win with `won=True`+contributor count, and **exactly once** under a double-resolve; strike fires per resolved blow but not on cooldown/no-active; and two **fail-open** guards proving a raising emit_objective/emit never disturbs the post/strike lifecycle). No schema; no faucet/sink; era-clean; no engine behavior change (telemetry is buffer-only + offline-flushed).

### 2026-06-21 — QA LOW+MED: +scene bad-arg error + summary size cap — *drop qa-scene-summary-caps* (Sonnet loop)
TWO delegated QA fixes from the 2026-06-20 break-it campaign. **LOW (`+scene <bad-arg>`):** `ctx.args.strip().isdigit()` returned False for negative IDs (`-1`), non-numeric strings (`abc`), floats (`3.5`), etc., so all non-positive-integer arguments silently fell through to "No active scene here." — making it impossible to tell whether you typed a bad ID or there was no scene. Fix: if `ctx.args` is non-empty and not a valid positive integer, return `"Invalid scene ID. Usage: +scene <id>"` instead of falling through. **MED (summary storage-DoS):** neither `+scene/summary`, `+plot/create`, nor `+plot/summary` had any server-side size cap — the QA repro stored a 100 KB plot summary. Applied a `MAX_SUMMARY_LEN = 4000` cap (matching the chargen background + mail generous-mid-point) at the storage seam of all three paths, with truncation (not rejection) and a user notice (mirroring the `qa-mail-body-cap` pattern). New `tests/test_qa_scene_bad_arg_and_summary_cap.py` (14: 5 bad-arg cases including valid id passes, 6 scene/plot summary-cap cases, 3 constant-value guards). No schema; era-clean; no faucet/sink.

### 2026-06-21 — QA MED: cap the in-game mail body (storage-DoS) — *drop qa-mail-body-cap*
The 2026-06-20 break-it campaign found in-game mail had **no server-side body size cap** — a single `@mail/quick` persisted a 262 KB body (ten ~2.6 MB) into the `mail` table, a cheap storage-DoS (chargen caps background at 2000; mail capped nothing). `MailCommand._do_send` — the single chokepoint every player mail path routes through (compose, `@mail/quick`, `@mail/reply` all call it) — now **truncates the body to `MAX_MAIL_BODY_LEN` (8000)** at the storage seam and notifies the sender. Generous enough for a multi-page letter, bounded against abuse; truncated (not rejected) so a long legitimate letter still sends. New `tests/test_qa_mail_body_cap.py` (3: oversized truncated + noticed, normal unchanged, cap generous-but-bounded). The companion `+scene`/`+plot` summary cap is delegated to a loop. No schema; era-clean.
### 2026-06-21 — QA HIGH: FP/CP/wound refunded on a mid-round disconnect — *drop qa-combat-disconnect-persist*
The 2026-06-20 break-it campaign found that `_apply_combat_wear`'s player post-round state save was gated on the session existing (`if sess and sess.character:`). A player who spent a **Force Point** or **Character Points** on a combat bonus and then **disconnected before the round resolved** had those points refunded on reconnect (an FP/CP-dup via disconnect), and the wound was lost. **Fix:** the authoritative `db.save_character(c.id, wound_level, character_points, force_points)` DB write now runs **ALWAYS** (keyed on `c.id`), independent of the session; only the in-memory session mirror + the PC-death hook still need a live session (so a disconnected player's spent points + wound persist to the DB). Mirrors the existing CP-persist / FP-persist fixes (this closes the disconnect window they left open). New `tests/test_qa_combat_disconnect_persist.py` (3 structural guards — this combat path is fixture-heavy, mirroring `tests/test_qa_rerun_findings.py` for the same persist class). 40 combat-regression tests green. **With this, all 3 QA-campaign HIGHs are fixed** (credit-integrity, kuat/kamino landing, this). No schema; era-clean; funnel-respecting.
### 2026-06-21 — Solo-PvE mob-grind reward trickle (v1) — *drop solo-pve-mob-grind*
Brian: players who want to "grind out some NPCs and zone out" when friends aren't on should get a small, satisfying reward without breaking advancement. Built the v1 (Brian chose option B). **Defeating an ORDINARY roaming hostile** (one with no other reward system today — not a bounty/anomaly/wilderness-creature/chain/vendor/intel NPC) now pays a **small daily-capped credit trickle + prestige**, and — per the EVE "ratting pays ISK + standings, never skillpoints" model — **ZERO character points** (advancement stays RP-primary; CP is the time/RP-gated skillpoint analog). New `engine/hunting_rewards.py`: `is_huntable_mob()` (a whitelist-inversion predicate — hostile AND none of the verified special-reward markers, so no double-reward), `on_huntable_kill()` (flat `BASE_REWARD=15` cr/kill via the `adjust_credits` funnel tag `mob_grind`, a `DAILY_SOFT_CAP=400` cr/day soft cap past which it drops to a token `OVER_CAP_FLOOR=3` — the "extreme trickle" tail, day-rolled), plus a per-character `hunting_log` (lifetime kill count) and earned milestone TITLES (25/100/500/2500 → the Hunter / Seasoned Hunter / Master Hunter / Apex Hunter). **Self-sinking:** a real fight's medical (50-1,000 cr) + repair cost exceeds the 15 cr trickle for any non-trivial mob, so the bounded faucet pairs with the existing combat-cost sinks. `engine/titles.py`: added `EARNED_TITLES` + `grant_earned_title()` (the no-charge "granted for deeds" III.2 extension the module's docstring anticipated — folded into `_BY_KEY` so worn-title display resolves; never in the +title BUY catalog). New `parser/hunting_commands.py` `+hunting` (read-only log view; day-rolls the daily meter for display). **★ Found + fixed a real seam bug:** the verify fan-out's code-review caught that DEAD-gated reward hooks placed inside `_apply_combat_wear` are **structurally inert** — `combat.resolve_round()` runs `_cleanup()` which **removes dead combatants before** `_apply_combat_wear` is called, so a DEAD NPC is never present in that loop. The mob-grind reward instead fires from a new `_award_mob_grind_rewards()` helper at **both** `resolve_round` call sites (normal + admin), which snapshots NPC combatants BEFORE resolution and rewards the killer for those that left combat at wound_level DEAD (the NPC db row survives death as `room_id=None`, so its ai_config is still readable). **⚠ The pre-existing `bounty`/`anomaly`/`WoW.3a`-Jedi-weight kill hooks in `_apply_combat_wear` share this inertness and likely never fired — flagged for a dedicated attended combat-hooks fix (see TODO).** New `tests/test_hunting_rewards.py` (23, incl. a **seam integration test** that drives `_award_mob_grind_rewards` end-to-end and proves a real kill pays the killer — and that survivors / special NPCs / offline killers do NOT — plus a no-character-points guard). Verify fan-out: invariant-auditor CLEAN (faucet bounded + self-sinking, funnel-routed, no CP, era-clean, phantom markers all real, no schema bump); the one code-review blocker (inert seam) + minor (stale daily-view) both fixed. 85 combat-regression tests green. No schema; era-clean.

### 2026-06-20 — Launch hardening: remove the deprecated datetime.utcnow() from mail/bounty timestamps — *drop datetime-utcnow-hardening*
`datetime.utcnow()` is deprecated (Python 3.12+) and slated for removal; the launch box runs **Python 3.14**, where the smoke run surfaced these as DeprecationWarnings. The three production sites that stamped mail/bounty `sent_at` (`engine/mail_utils.py:69`, `parser/mail_commands.py:333`, `parser/pc_bounty_commands.py:239`) now use the **behavior-preserving** `datetime.now(timezone.utc).replace(tzinfo=None).isoformat()` — the stored string stays **byte-identical** (naive-UTC ISO, no `+00:00` offset), so existing rows, `datetime.fromisoformat` parsing, the `[:10]` date-slice, and string `ORDER BY sent_at` are all unaffected (verified: 347 mail/bounty tests green). Chose naive-preserving over a tz-aware switch specifically to avoid mixing offset/no-offset formats in the existing `mail.sent_at` column. New `tests/test_datetime_utcnow_hardening.py` (3: no `utcnow()` anywhere in engine/parser/server/db/ai production code, the 3 sites use the naive-UTC pattern, and the pattern is format-preserving/parseable). No schema; era-clean; no faucet/sink.

New `engine/contextual_hints.py`: a `HINTS` map from resolved `cmd.key` → `(hint_key, guide_slug, nudge_text)` for **combat** (`attack` → Ground Combat), **shops** (`shop`/`buy`/`sell` → Player Shops), **crafting** (`craft` → Crafting), and **inter-world travel** (`land` → Space & Systems); and `maybe_emit_first_hit_hint(session, db, char, cmd_key)`, which fires **at most once per subsystem per character** via a new `seen_hints` map (a top-level sibling of `tutorial_chain` in the character `attributes` blob, persisted through the canonical `chain_events._persist_attrs` — never a `force_sensitive` kwarg). Producer seam: `parser/commands.py CommandParser._execute`, in the existing post-execute block alongside the CW-tutorial command hook, matching on the **resolved `cmd.key`** so aliases (kill/att/shoot/dock) normalize — and fully best-effort (a hint failure can never break the command). Delivery: a sys-event pose (`make_system_event` → `session.send_json('pose_event', …)`) — a banner row on the web client, a plain styled line on Telnet (the existing send_json sys-event fallback), so the nudge works on both protocols and the bare-`help` it points at opens the in-game guide browser on web / the help system on Telnet. The nudge **emits before marking seen**, so a transient delivery failure re-fires next time rather than marking the player "seen" for a hint they never got. New `tests/test_npe_contextual_hints.py` (10: first-hit emits + marks seen, no re-emit, shop/buy/sell share one subsystem, untracked cmd no-op, persist writes only `attributes`, four distinct subsystems each fire once, pre-existing attrs preserved, best-effort swallows a throwing transport, every hint slug is a real guide, hook wired in dispatch). Verify fan-out (invariant-auditor + code-reviewer) clean; the one reviewer MINOR (emit/mark ordering) folded in. No schema; era-clean; no faucet/sink.
### 2026-06-20 — NPE: stop the post-combat "huge text" — split the room-contents NPC name/description line — *drop npe-npc-desc-not-posed*
Closed the DEFERRED NPE item the prior session couldn't pin down ("a defeated NPC re-poses its FULL physical description in the brighter/larger pose style"). **It was never a server pose emitter** — it's a client mis-classification of a server line. `LookCommand._look_room_contents` (`parser/builtin_commands.py`) emitted a present NPC as a single line `  <Name> is here. <description>`. The web client's text classifier (`static/client.html` `simplePoseMatch`) parses that as name=`<Name>`, verb=`is`, rest=`here. <description>` and — once the NPC is a **known actor** (it posed during combat, so `rememberActorName` added it) — renders the whole thing as a bright `.pose-body` NPC *pose* row instead of dim desc text. The "defeat" trigger was incidental: combat makes the NPC a known actor, then a reflexive/auto `look` re-renders room contents and the desc gets posed. **Fix (both halves, best/most-complete):** (1) **server** — split the line so `  <Name> is here.` is on its own line and the description goes to a separate wrapped line via `session.send_prose(desc, indent="    ")`, mirroring the already-safe `LookCommand._look_at` NPC branch; once the desc isn't appended to the name, the `is here.` line is too short (< the regex's 8-char tail) to match `simplePoseMatch` at all. (2) **client (defense-in-depth)** — `classifyAndAppend` now computes `isPresenceLine` (verb ∈ {is,are,was,were} + remainder starts with `here`) and excludes it from the pose branch, so any other emitter of a `<Name> is here …` line is also safe. The condensed (≥5 NPCs) path was already immune (names only, no desc). JS re-validated via `node --check` (exit 0). New `tests/test_npe_npc_desc_not_posed.py` (5: name+desc never share a line, name line present+short, desc still shown, bracket-desc still suppressed, client guard present). 130 look-path regression tests green (pvp/bond markers, corpses, look/examine, vanity titles). Telnet unaffected (no client classifier). No schema; era-clean; `parser/builtin_commands.py` + `static/client.html` only.
### 2026-06-20 — NPE: interface tour fires per-character + teaches the in-game GUIDES button — *drop npe-tour-per-character*
The first-run interface tour (coach-marks over the command bar, quick actions, objective, training panel) was gated by a single global `localStorage` flag (`m3_onboard_tour_done`) — so once dismissed on any character, it never showed again on that browser. Brian's playtest: "we had a more robust onboarding that walked the player through the UI — I didn't see it this time" (his dev browser had the flag set from an earlier character). Fixes (`static/client.html`, additive): (1) the tour gate is now **keyed per character** (`_tourKey()` → `m3_onboard_tour_done_<character_id>`) so every new character gets the tour once — a returning player making a fresh character, and a dev cycling test characters, both see it again; (2) a new coach-mark teaches the **GUIDES button** (the in-game help browser shipped in the prior drop — "GUIDES, or just type help, opens the field guides without leaving the game"). `endOnboardTour` persists the per-character key. JS re-validated via `node --check` (exit 0). New `tests/test_onboard_tour_per_character.py` (2 guards: per-character key + guide coach-mark). Era-clean; no schema; no server change. (Deferred: the post-combat "huge text" — a defeated NPC re-posing its full description — needs a live repro to pinpoint the server emitter.)
### 2026-06-20 — In-game guide browser: surface the 25 long-form guides inside /play — *drop in-game-guide-browser*
Players can now read all field guides without leaving the game client. Added to `static/client.html` (additive only): a `renderGuideMarkdown()` function ported verbatim from `portal.html`; a `#guide-overlay` two-column modal (category/guide list left, reading pane right) matching the `.chargen-overlay` pattern; `openGuideBrowser()` / `closeGuideBrowser()` / `loadGuideIntoPane(slug)` with a cached index fetch and graceful error handling; a `sendCmd` intercept that opens the browser for `guide`, `guides`, `+guide`, `+guides`, or bare `help` (with-args `help <topic>` still goes to server); a GUIDE button in the quick-action row (`.qa-btn guide-qa-btn`); and all four functions exported on `window` for inline-onclick use. CSS block (`.guide-overlay`, `.guide-modal`, `.guide-list-col`, `.guide-read-col`, `.guide-md` h1-h4/p/ul/li/code/pre/table/blockquote/a) adapted from portal `.md-body` for the dark terminal theme. Uses existing `/api/portal/guides` and `/api/portal/guide/{slug}` endpoints — no new server code. JS syntax verified via `node --check` (exit 0). ### 2026-06-20 — Nano map alignment: Jedi Temple garden pin now sits on the painted greenhouse — *drop nano-align-jedi-temple-2026-06-20*
First of the Nano interior-map alignment pass (Brian 2026-06-20: "use your reasoning to take a hard look at where you're placing things on the map and make sure they make sense"). The painted Jedi Temple floorplan put the greenhouse at the `(1.2, 4.8)` grid cell, but the layout coded the **Meditation Garden** at `(1.2, 3.0)` and **Medical Bay** at `(1.2, 4.8)` — so the nav overlay labelled a plain room "Garden" and stamped "Medical Bay" on the actual greenhouse (the pins are anchored to room coordinates, the painting is not). Fixed by swapping the two rooms' grid positions, the garden landmark pin, and the two entrance-hall→room corridors that feed them — so the Garden label lands on the painted garden and Medical Bay on the plain cell below. Verified with a new coordinate-grid probe tool (`tools/_grid_probe.py`, draws the room grid + labels over the substrate so placement can be checked by eye rather than guessed). The other two wired interiors (Coruscant Works — glowing reactor=Power Grid, tanks=Atmospheric Plant; Gladiator Barracks — weapon-rack room=Armory, Den up top) were probe-checked and already coherent, so only Jedi Temple needed the swap.
